164 2020 Annual Report PT Bank Negara Indonesia (Persero) Tbk Uniting Energy to Revive the CountryReview of the Economy and   Banking Industry  The Global economy  In 2020, most countries in the world instituted various  forms of lock down policy to cope with the Coronavirus  Disease 2019 (Covid-19) pandemic.
The lock down policies  resulted in restricted mobility in a global scale, which led to  declining consumption, stoppage of production processes,  reduction of international trade and, eventually, contraction  of the global economy.
A number of international organizations have predicted a  contraction of global economic growth in 2020 of -5.2%  to -3.7% yoy.
While the Covid-19 pandemic has yet to  end, many countries in the world have begun to cautiously  move the wheels of economic activities, while some  others remained in a lock down in order to better protect BNI has compiled an implementation  timeline for various strategic initiatives over the next five years into the 2019-2023 Corporate Plan.
In line with the 2019-2023 BNI Corporate Plan, in 2020 the Bank will enter the business expansion through digital corporate and retail ecosystem phase.
Management   Discussion & Analysis 165 Uniting Energy to Revive the Country2020 Annual Report PT Bank Negara Indonesia (Persero) TbkThe China’s economy managed a positive growth of 1.9%  (yoy) in 2020 amidst the contraction of global economies.
The positive growth of the economy was the result of  a strict policy of total lockdown in the epicenter of the  pandemic, fiscal stimulus package for China’s domestic  industries, and effective social assistance program for  citizens impacted by the pandemic.
In 2021, China’s  economy is predicted to rebound to a growth of 8.2%  (yoy) on the strength returning manufacturing activities,  people mobility, and increasing global demand for China’s  products.
The IMF predicted that Japan’s economy in 2020 will  suffer a contraction of -5.4% on account of the Covid-19  pandemic.
In 2021, Japan’s economy is predicted to  rebound with a positive growth of 2.3% (yoy), in line  with the recovery of Japan’s Manufacturing PMI and  improvement in the country’s trade balance in 2021.
Global economic growth in 2021 is predicted to recover  under several assumptions, including the control of the  Covid-19 pandemic, recovery of  the labor market, recovery  of industrial performance, improved retail sales, and  increased trading volume.
Global economic Growth (%, yoy) 2018 2019 2020 F 2021 F 2022 F World Output 3.5 2.8 -4.4 5.2 4.2 United States 3.0 2.2 -4.3 3.1 3.1 Euro Area 1.8 1.3 -8.3 5.2 2.9 Japan 0.3 0.7 -5.3 2.3 1.7 China 6.8 6.1 1.9 8.2 5.8 IndonesIa’s economy  Indonesia’s economy has experienced a slowdown since  2019 and went into a contraction in 2020 as an impact  of Covid-19 pandemic.
Indonesia’s economic growth for  2019 was 5.02%, while in 2020 was -2.07% (BPS, 2021).
The outbreak of the Covid-19 pandemic was followed by  a lockdown policy of various forms in many countries of  the world, and called the Large-Scale Social Restriction  (PSBB) policy in Indonesia, which restricted the mobility of  people and goods and led to the decline in consumption/ demand, production and investment.
Indonesia’s economic  slowdown has occurred since 2019 mainly as a result of  the trade war between the United States and China.
the lives of citizens.
Nearing the end of the year 2020, the global economy has slowly begun to recover to its pre- pandemic levels, with activities conducted in observance  of health protocols.
In 2021, global economic growth is predicted to rebound  in a positive way and take the form of a “V-shape” at  the level of 4.2% -5.2% (yoy).
The improvement in the  global economy, among others, will be supported by the  vaccination drive that will be given globally starting in Q1- 2021 and is expected to be a game changer.
Vaccination is  expected to result in a herd immunity, making the global  community “immune” from Covid-19, returning global  mobility and encouraging global economic recovery.
World GdP Growth (yoy) 2020 F 2021 F 2022 F Bloomberg -3.7% 5.1% 4.1% OECD -4.2% 4.2% 3.7% IMF -4.4% 5.2% 4.2% World Bank -5.2% 4.2% N/A economy by ReGIon The International Monetary Fund (IMF) predicted that the  United States (US) economy in 2020 will grow at -4.3%  (yoy).
A number of factors led to the expected contraction  in the economy, including the rampant outbreak of  Covid-19 pandemic, racial riots in mid-year, as well as  instability in domestic political front during the US general  elections process in 2020.
For the year 2021, the US  economy is predicted to grow positively by 3.1% (yoy).
The  official policies of the new US president-elect, Joe Biden,  in 2021 will focus on controlling the Covid-19 pandemic  and promoting US economic recovery through the “Made  in America” program, much like Trump’s “America First”  economic policy.
In the Euro-Zone, weak performance in the tourism and  manufacturing sectors is predicted to result in 8.3%  (yoy) contraction of the economy in 2020.
The economic  contraction is exacerbated by lockdown policy taken in a number of Euro Zone countries, as well as the threat from  a new Covid-19 variant appearing in the UK near the end  of 2020.
The IMF predicted that in 2021, the Euro Zone  economies would grow by 4.2% (yoy).  166 2020 Annual Report PT Bank Negara Indonesia (Persero) Tbk Uniting Energy to Revive the CountryControlling Covid-19, along with the implementation of  the National Economic Recovery (PEN) program and  the Omnibus Law on Job Creation, are the keys to  economic recovery in 2021.
Domestic demand in terms  of consumption and investment still remains as the  primary driver of national economic growth post-Covid-19  pandemic.
Implementation of the Omnibus Law on Job  Creation is expected to attract more overseas investors  to invest their capital in Indonesia.
Government spending  is directed towards supporting the momentum of growth,  continuing with the countercyclical policy, and accelerating  the PEN program post-Covid-19.
Exports are predicted  to improve in line with the recovery of global economies,  as well as efforts by the Government in expanding the  potential export destination countries and in developing the  tourism sector.
Indonesia’s economy is expected to rebound in 2021, with  the IMF predicting an economic growth of 4.8% (yoy).
The availability of the Covid-19 vaccine raises hopes for  an increasingly significant economic recovery.
On the  other hand, the application of the Omnibus Law on the  Job Creation Law since it was passed in November 2020  is also expected to have an impact on the attractiveness  of investment that also encourages Indonesia’s economic  growth.
Inflation level throughout 2020 tended to decline compared  with those in 2019 as consumer purchases weakened  due to the Covid-19 pandemic.
The pandemic, and the  social restrictions that follow, have resulted in a weakening  of consumer demand as well as purchasing power.
Certain inflation-forming components, such as volatile  foodstuffs and goods, contributed significantly to the  decline in inflation throughout 2020.
The low inflation rates throughout 2020 was mainly driven by inflation in several  expenditure groups, such as the food and beverage,  transportation, information and communications, housing,  water and electricity, as well as personal care and other  services.
Inflation in 2021 is estimated to remain at the 3%  - 4% level.
Observing economic developments in 2020, Bank  Indonesia has lowered its benchmark interest rates, the  BI-7 Day Reverse Repo Rate (BI7DRRR), by 125 bps or  5 times to 3.75%.
Reductions were made in February,  March, June, July, and November 2020, respectively, each  of 25 bps.
This decision is consistent with the forecast for inflation to remain low and external stability that is maintained to promote economic recovery during the  Covid-19 pandemic.
Meanwhile, in April, May, August,  September, October and December 2020, Bank Indonesia  continued to maintain the BI7DRRR with the consideration  of maintaining external stability, amidst the predicted  low inflation rate.
Until 2021, Bank Indonesia is expected  to maintain low interest rates until there are signs of  increasing inflationary pressure.
In 2021, the BI7DRRR is  estimated to be in the 3.75% - 4% range.
The profusion of fiscal stimulus in the developed  economies in 2021 will tend to strengthen the Rupiah  against the US Dollar.
In 2020, the Rupiah was under  significant pressure, as sentiments of the weakening  effect of Covid-19 pandemic on Indonesia’s economy  drove foreign investors sell off their holdings in Indonesia  and place them in safe haven assets.
In 2021, a number of developed countries such as Japan  and the US have stated that they will provide a jumbo  stimulus package.
The US Government and Senate have  agreed on a 2021 stimulus package worth US$900 billion.
The Japanese Government has also launched a stimulus  package totaling 73.6 trillion Yen or US$708 billion.
The  Central Bank of Japan said it would buy securities from  the market indefinitely.
The Fed has repeatedly stated  the need for stimulus and it is likely that the White House  will approve of the Fed proposal that President Trump  previously ignored.
From Europe, the EU Central Bank  has approved the purchase of securities from the market  worth Rp3,080 trillion until 2022.
At the same time, the  development of the Covid-19 vaccine will be closer to  certainty.
Therefore, it is estimated that capital inflow will  again enter the Emerging Market, including Indonesia, so that the Rupiah exchange rate will be better in 2021.
In  2021, the Rupiah exchange rate will move in the range of  Rp13,500-14,500 per US Dollar.
Vaccination will be a Game Changer for economic recovery,  as vaccination is hoped to lead to the so-called herd  immunity.
With communities being  “immune” from  Covid-19, global mobility can return to normal and thus  encourage the recovery of economic activities.
Review of the Economy and Banking Industry Management   Discussion & Analysis 167 Uniting Energy to Revive the Country2020 Annual Report PT Bank Negara Indonesia (Persero) TbkbankInG IndusTR y oveR vIeW  During the Covid-19 Pandemic, growth in banks’ third- party funds (DPK) rose far higher than the growth in  banks’ loans.
LDR, NIM, ROA decreased while banking  NPL increased.
CAR is still maintained at the level of  24.25%.
Until November 2020, the growth of third party  funds (DPK) reached 11.5% (yoy), higher than the growth  in deposits a year earlier in the same period which was  only 6.72% (yoy).
On the other hand, loans disbursed  contracted by -1.39% (yoy), much lower than in November  2019, which grew by 7.05% (yoy).
The high growth in third party funds was influenced by  the increasing tendency to save the public to banks to  anticipate the risk of economic downturn, especially  for large bank groups.
In addition, the placement of  funds by the Government in the framework of the  National Economic Recovery (PEN) program has also  become a catalyst for the growth of third party funds in national banking.
Meanwhile, from the loan side, the  low demand for loan was influenced by the weakening  economy exposed to the Covid-19 pandemic, so that  business players chose not to expand (low loan demand)  accompanied by banking prudence in controlling non- performing loans.
As Indonesia’s economic recovery progresses in 2021, loan  growth is projected to improve, particularly consumption  loan and working capital loan, which are estimated to grow  5% -6% yoy.
This loan growth will be supported by third  party funds which are estimated to grow in the range of  7% -9% yoy in 2021.
busIness PRosPecTs  In 3rd Quarter 2020, the largest contributors to GDP  by economic sector are the manufacturing sector at  19.62%; followed by the agriculture, forestry & fisheries  sector at 14.68% and the trading sector at 12.83%.
The  manufacturing, agriculture, forestry & fisheries, and trading  sectors are predicted to remain as prospective industries in  2021 in line with the improving Indonesian economy.
The manufacturing sector registered a contraction of -4.3%  (yoy) in the 3rd Quarter 2020.
The sector is predicted to  grow by 4.7% - 5.5% in 2021.
Prospective sub-sectors  in the manufacturing sector are the chemical industry, pharmaceuticals and traditional medicine, food and  beverage, and basic metal industry.
The agriculture, forestry & fisheries sector grew by 2.15%  (yoy) in 3rd Quarter 2020.
The sector is predicted to grow  by 3.3% - 3.9% in 2021.
Prospective sub-sectors in the  agriculture, forestry & fisheries sector are food crops,  horticulture crops, and plantation crops.
The trading sector registered a decline of -5.03% in 3rd  Quarter 2020.
The sector is predicted to grow by 4.3% -  5.3% in 2021.
Prospective sub-sectors in the trading sector  are vehicle and non-vehicle trading.
In 3rd Quarter 2020, highest GDP growth was recorded  by the Health Services sector with 15.33%, followed by  the Information & Communications sector with 10.61% (yoy).
The Health Services sector is predicted to remain  prospective in 2021 with a projected growth rate of 4.6% -  6.1% (yoy), in line with the mass vaccination process that  will be carried out throughout the year 2021.
Likewise, the  Information & Communications sector is projected to grow  by 8.3% - 10.1% (yoy).

Acting as a founder of the pension fund and pension fund manager in accordance with the provisions of the  laws and regulations;oPeRa TIonal RevIeW PeR busIness  and GeoGRaPhIcal seGmenTs  BNI conducts its business and activities in the banking sector in accordance with the Articles of Association as  set forth in Deed No. 52, dated May 22, 2018.
Its main  activities	are: 1.
Raising funds from the public in the form of deposits  such as demand deposits, time deposits, certificate of  deposits, savings deposits, and/or other equivalent; 2.
Issuing debt instruments; 172 2020 Annual Report PT Bank Negara Indonesia (Persero) Tbk Uniting Energy to Revive the Country23.
Conducting financial services, commercial banking, and other investment banking; 24.
Performing other activities commonly conducted by the bank that are not contrary to legislation.
In addition to those key activities, BNI also performs business support activities in optimizing available resources in support  of the core business activities, that are not contrary to legislation.
The	Bank’s	operating	segments	are	divided	based	on	the	main	customer	groups	and	products,	as	follows:	Corporate,	 Medium and Small, Consumer, Treasury and Financial Institutions, Head Office and Subsidiaries.
In determining segment  results, the accounts of assets and liabilities and related revenues and expenses are attributed to each segment based on  management’s internal reporting policies.
Transactions between business segments are treated like third party transactions,  which are recorded under each segment and eliminated at the Bank level.
In	summary,	each	reporting	per	segment	in	the	Banks	segment	reporting	is	as	follows:	 •		corporations:	including	loans,	customer	deposits	and	other	transactions	for	corporate	customers.
•		medium and small:	including	loans,	customer	deposits	and	other	transactions	for	small	to	medium	scale	customers.
•		consumer: includes consumer financing loans, including housing loans, credit cards and other transactions for  consumer customers.
•		Treasury and Financial Institutions:	related	to	the	Bank’s	treasury	activities	including	foreign	exchange	transactions,	 money market, capital market and fixed income, including among others the international banking business and  overseas branches.
•		head office:	is	the	centralized	provision	of	services	to	other	segments.
•		subsidiaries: all transactions conducted by Subsidiaries that are engaged in sharia banking, insurance, consumer  financing and securities.

deposit/Third Party Funds Discussions related to strategy, productivity, business  prospects and achievement strategies for BNI’s Corporate  Segment - Deposits/Third Party Funds (TPF) in 2020 are as  follows: description of corporate segment - TPF Third Party Funds (TPF) in the corporate segment (Business Banking) are deposits from institutional  (non-individuals) customers managed by the Corporate  segment.
TPF in the Corporate segment is divided into 5  (five) sub-segments, namely the SOE, Non-Bank Financial  Institutions (NBFI), Ministries/Institutions, Universities, and  Area segments.
Scope of management of Corporate TPF is divided into 2  (two)	amounts,	namely: 1.
Managing and developing BNI business in the  Business Banking sector, both in the corporate and  area segments (regions and branches). 2.
The business focus of Corporate – TPF business is to fulfill all the needs of Business Banking customers,  end to end, both B2B and B2C.

The upselling  strategy of corporate customers is expected to  increase the product holding ratio of customers in  terms of transactional, deposit or financing products.

other Transactions  Discussions related to strategies, productivity, business  prospects and strategies for BNI Corporate Segment -  Other	Transactions	in	2020	are	as	follow: description of corporate segment - other  Transactions in 2020  For Corporate Segment customers, BNI offers its flagship  products such as BNI Cash Management, which allows  customers to independently manage their corporate cash  flow more regularly and are monitored online.
Features in  the BNI Cash Management product include overbooking  transfers, domestic and international inter-bank transfers,  online tax payment, virtual account for collections,  payment of bills through bill payment, and supply chain  financing.
With cash management transactions, TPF will grow continuously and thus indirectly also maintaining liquidity  at BNI.
The primary application provided by BNI that can  be used by customers to conduct Cash Management  transactions is known as BNIDirect.
BNIDirect is a web-based application that has been securely tested and can  be accessed via the internet from anywhere, anytime,  and using any media.
The BNIDirect website could be  accessed	at	https://bnidirect.
BNIDirect	can	be	 accessed via a computer or cellphone connected to the  internet network.
Also available now is BNIDirect Mobile,  which is very flexible and easy to install on every type of  mobile phone.
corporate segment - other Transactions strategies  in 2020 Throughout 2020, BNI implemented strategies to increase  transactions	in	cash	management,	as	follow: 1.
Maintaining and acquiring SOE/Corporate Customers  who have significant ecosystems. 2.
Exploring and identifying the potential for Non-Tax State Revenue (PNBP) and the expenditure flows in  Government Ministries/Institutions in order to offer  possible business solutions.  3.
Exploring and identifying derivative businesses and value chains from corporate customers in order to  provide close loop transaction solutions. 4.
Expanding the scope of transaction access to the commercial customer segment by optimizing the  potential of BNI debtors in each region.

small segment – loan  Discussions related to description, strategy, productivity, prospect and strategy for Small Segment – Loan in 2020 is  presented	below: description of small segment – loans  The Small segment manages productive loan facility of up  to Rp15 billion for individual customers, businesses and  business groups.
small segment – loan Performance in 2020 The Small segment managed to maintain loan growth in  the double-digit range in the midst of Covid-19 pandemic.
As at 31 December 2020, loans in the Small segment  amounted to Rp84.8 trillion, up by 12.4%, or Rp9.34  trillion, from the previous year.
The growth is driven by  KUR product with growth of 33.4%, and non-KUR products  with growth of 2.3%.
Disbursement of People’s Business Credit (KUR) in 2020  amounted to Rp21.3 trillion for 239,536 debtors.
This  represents a 21.1% increase from KUR disbursement in  the previous year.
Some 51.2% of the KUR disbursement  in 2020 is directed at productive sectors that include the  agriculture sector, fisheries sector, manufacturing sector,  and services sector, and thus is expected to help energize  the real sector of the economy.
In 2020, interest and sharia income – net in the Medium  segment amounted to Rp2.5 trillion, down 28.2% from  the amount recorded in 2019 at Rp3.5 trillion.
In 2020,  the Medium segment also set aside a higher level of  provision for impairment losses at Rp5.9 trillion, or an  increase of 361.6% over the amount in 2019, to anticipate  the impact of Covid-19 pandemic.
As a result, operating profits of the Medium segment registered a loss of Rp3.6  trillion, compared with profits of Rp1.8 trillion in 2019.
This  reflected the management strategy to increase the loan  loss provision due to Covid-19 pandemic.
medium segment – loan Prospects and strategies The year 2020 was a dynamic year for the Medium  segment, with the priority on recovery strategy being  a logical initiative alongside preparations of strategic  initiatives for 2021.
A number of credible domestic and  international institutions have predicted that Indonesia’s  economy will grow by 5%-6% in 2021, with loan growth of  7.5% for all segments.
Based on those projections as well as the condition of  the loan portfolio in 2020, the Medium segment have  determined growth targets in 2021 with a priority on the  gradual replacement of portfolios that no longer provide  optimum yields to BNI.
Initiatives will also be taken to  strengthen and refine the credit processes through the  implementation of tools with digital capability in order to  improve the management and quality of the loan portfolio  in the Medium segment.
Overall, in 2021, the Medium segment will be present as a  provider of holistic solutions for the MSME customers and  ecosystem,	through	6	(six)	strategies,	namely: 1.
Corporate Value Chain.
The Medium segment will  increase the portion of financing to business partners  of selected corporate customers in order towards  quality loan expansion. 2.
The Medium segment will promote the development of business ecosystems  that can generate closed-loop transactions and  increased Fee-Based Income.

consumer segment-loans  Consumer loan products consist of mortgage loans, credit  card, payroll-based loans, and others. 1.
mortgage  BNI Griya is a loan facility intended for individuals  who wants to own residential properties, apartments,  shops/houses and villas, both new or second-hand.
Through the BNI Griya Multiguna program, this facility  can also be used to purchase plots of land, or for  house construction, renovation, refinancing, takeovers,  and loan top up.2.
Payroll based loan  BNI Fleksi is an Unsecured Loan product from BNI  available to active employees and retirees whose  payment of salaries and retirement benefits is made  through BNI. 3.
credit card  Credit cards are one of the consumer loan products as a payment using a card that can be used by individuals  and corporations to make payments. 4.
bnI Instan  BNI Instan is a loan product with BNI Deposits,  Savings or Current Accounts, as well as securities  (Government Bonds/ORI) as collateral.

bnI Griya In 2020, BNI Griya’s portfolio amounted to Rp46.0 trillion,  or a growth of 4.33% from the position in 2019.
BNI  Griya’s expansion of Rp3.4 trillion was focused on the  primary property market segment through collaboration  with property developers and online property media, as  well as the secondary property segment market through  property agents.
In addition, BNI also participated in the  Million Homes Program initiated by the Ministry of Public  Works and Public Housing in the disbursement Mortgage  subsidies in the form of FLPP , SSB and BP2BT facilities  totalling Rp5.4 trillion.
bnI Griya strategy in 2020  The Covid-19 pandemic in 2020 have had an impact on  consumer demand for property products.
However, BNI  managed to maintain positive growth as well as improve  its market position through the implementation of the  following	programs	and	strategies: •	 Disbursement	of	BNI	Griya	in	the	primary	property	 market through strategic partnership with property developers and in the secondary property market  through the optimization of existing mortgage  customers, while providing convenient and fast loan  application process for potential debtors, and also  organizing online customer gathering events with BNI  Emerald customers and Top Developers to increase  acquisition of BNI Griya application.
•	 Focusing	the	marketing	of	BNI	Griya	to	customers	 in the fixed-income segment, while optimizing the  role of branches, especially in the major cities, to  facilitate the loan process.
Also, creating synergy with Business Banking (Corporate, Medium and Small)  and with subsidiaries, to provide banking services for  employees of BNI’s institutional partners, including  construction loans to property developers.
•	 BNI	 was	also	active	in	driving	the	digital	transformation	 with regard to BNI Griya loan application, especially in  times of limited mobility during the periods of Large  Scale Social Restriction (PSBB) and PSBB Transition,  by providing an online access for consumers to apply  for a mortgage loan through the e-Form application,  and by organizing the Griya Expo Virtual housing  exhibition event in cooperation with Rumah.
com with  nation-wide and even regional (Southeast Asia) reach.
In addition, BNI Griya also offers affordable installment  facility through the Angsuran Suka-Suka feature with  effective fixed interest rates of 4.74% p.
for one year and 6.74% p.
for two years, a grace period of  2 years maximum, Instant Approval process for Top  Developers, and loan tenor of up to 30 years.
support for Government Programs BNI is always active in supporting the government program  to provide housing for low-income communities (MBR)  through the channeling of Housing Financing Liquidity  Facilities (FLPP) funds in collaboration with the Ministry  of Public Works and Public Housing.
In 2020, BNI held a  virtual mass contract of KPR Sejahtera BNI FLPP facility,  offering low down payments, affordable installments and  an installment period of up to 20 years, to potential debtors  in the MBR segment.

bnI Instan  BNI Instan is a Cash Collateral Credit product for  customers of BNI, offering a loan facility secured with the  customer’s deposits at BNI (time deposit accounts/current  accounts/savings accounts), or with liquid Government  Bonds instruments (SUN) such as Retail Government Bond  (ORI) and Retail Sukuk (SR) with Fixed Rate (FR) or Variable  Rate (VR), except Savings Sukuk (ST) and Retail Savings  Bonds (SBR), that the customers can purchase from BNI,  other banks or securities companies as Sales Agents, and  kept in the Sub-Registry as regulated.
bnI Instan strategy in 2020  The expansion strategy for BNI Instan in 2020 focused  on the disbursement of facilities to existing debtors and  facilitating the booking process with the support of a digital  platform.
bnI Instan strategy for 2021 BNI Instan will still be positioned as one of the drivers of  third party funds retention, with focus on facilitating the  booking process through partner institutions, customers in  the SOE, Corporate, Government Ministries, and University  188 2020 Annual Report PT Bank Negara Indonesia (Persero) Tbk Uniting Energy to Revive the Countrysectors, as well as existing customers and employees of  selected partners, supported by digital enhancement and  development of product features.
credit card  BNI credit card is a consumer loan product to be used by  individual and corporate customers to conduct a payment  for a variety of financial transactions such as when making  a shopping purchase or for cash withdrawals.
BNI credit  card	products	comprise	of: 1.
Regular	Credit	Card,	which	consists	of:	BNI	Visa	Silver,	 BNI Mastercard Silver, BNI Visa Gold, BNI Mastercard Gold and BNI JCB Gold. 2.
Premium	Credit	Cards,	which	consist	of:	BNI	Style	 Titanium, BNI Visa Platinum, BNI American Express  Business Card, BNI JCB Precious, BNI Mastercard  World, Visa Signature, and BNI Visa Infinite. 3.
Co-Branding Credit Card, which consists of BNI-LOTTE Mart, BNI-Garuda, BNI-Pertamina, BNI-Telkomsel, BNI- Bank bjb, and BNI-Bank DKI. 4.
Affinity	Credit	Card,	which	consist	of:	University	 Cards, Alumni Association Cards, and Community  Cards such as BNI WWF Credit Cards and BNI Harley Owners Group. 5.
Corporate	Credit	Card,	which	consists	of:	BNI	Visa	 Corporate Card Gold, BNI Visa Corporate Card  Platinum. 6.
Private	Label	Credit	Card,	which	consist	of:	BNI	 Traveling Card, BNI Gasoline Card, and BNI Health  Card. 7.
BNI Cash Card is an unsecured, revolving loan product that can be converted into fixed installments, and can  only be used to make cash withdrawals at ATMs or  tellers.
credit card – strategy 2020  With the tag line “Starts from the Card”, BNI Credit Card  business focuses on efforts to maintain market share  in the industry, amidst the Covid-19 pandemic that has  occurred since early 2020.
Several initiatives have been made to maintain product positioning and market share in  the	credit	card	industry,	as	follows: 1.
Increase credit card portfolio growth using the  Extended Installment and Balance Conversion strategy  on selected cardholders. 2.
Increase credit card sales volume growth with a focus on increasing transaction volume both merchants  and features, as well as strengthening e-commerce  transactions with a focus on top strategic e-commerce  partners.3.
Increase credit card sales volume growth with a focus on “Lifestyle Experience” transactions. 4.
Maximizing partnerships with strategic e-commerce merchants (market place). 5.
Focus on promos at Groceries, Dining and Healthcare category merchants as well as further initiatives  following the “new normal” economic recovery  phase. 6.
Increasing the contribution of credit card sales volumes in all regions/regions through cooperation  with local strategic merchants. 7.
Increase credit card transactions through merchant promos in various regions/locales at 13 Regional Offices in accordance with the “new normal”  economic recovery phase including optimization of  e-commerce transactions at local merchants. 8.
Implement contactless or touchless credit card use in order to increase security and convenience for  customers in conducting transactions without making  physical contact with the EDC terminal. 9.
Developing digital-based credit card acquisitions through the digital signature mechanism. 10.
Increase credit card acquisition by optimizing captive and non-captive customer data leads for selected  cardholder, as well as bundling and cross selling  programs for consumer products and business  banking. 11.
Developing Transactional Features and Services on the BNI Credit Card Mobile application. 12.
Mitigating and managing credit risk through an  asset quality improvement program and providing  convenience for credit card payments, especially for  Covid-19 -affected cardholders.
credit card – Performance in 2020  The credit card business is one of the businesses affected  by the Covid-19 pandemic, due to the decline in retail  transactions as a result of social restrictions in various  regions.
The outstanding growth and increase in credit  card sales volume during the pandemic in 2020 was quite  under pressure.
However, BNI was still able to maintain  the decline in the credit card business under the industry  average.
As of December 2020, the decline in BNI’s credit  card outstanding compared to last year’s achievement was  minus 9.3%, while the industry declined by minus 15.6%.
BNI continues to strive to increase credit card transactions  during the pandemic, with a promotion strategy that is in  accordance with the ‘new normal’ condition and health  protocols set by the government.

deposit/Third Party Funds BNI has a variety of customer deposit products to meet the needs of all customers, including savings and time  deposits products.
In 2020, BNI has the following deposit  products: savings  BNI	savings	products	come	in	several	variants,	as	follow:1.
Saving Account Plus (Taplus), is a savings account  that provides PLUS services with various features and  benefits. 2.
Taplus Bisnis, is a savings product intended for business and non-business players, both individuals  and non-individuals, equipped with features and  facilities that provide convenience and flexibility in  supporting business ventures. 3.
TAPPA (Taplus Pegawai/Anggota), is a savings product intended for employees/members of a company/ institution/association/professional organization that  collaborates with BNI, which functions as a means of  savings and as employee/member identity cards. 4.
Taplus Muda, is a savings product in the form of savings intended for young people ranging in age from  17 (seventeen) to 35 (thirty five) years. 5.
Taplus Anak, a savings product to help teach children  to save from an early age, intended for children under  17 (seventeen) years of age. 6.
Emerald Saving, is a savings product for Emerald segment customers (Personal, Priority and Private  Banking). 190 2020 Annual Report PT Bank Negara Indonesia (Persero) Tbk Uniting Energy to Revive the Country7.
BNI Dollars, a type of deposit in foreign currency  (USD/SGD/AUD) which has a more stable exchange  rate and provides convenience in transactions. 8.
Tapenas, is a time deposit to assist financial planning to achieve future goals with more certainty. 9.
Simpanan Pelajar (SimPel), is a savings product for PAUD, TK, SD, SMP , SMA, Madrasah (MI, MTs, MA)  students or equivalent that are issued nationally by  banks in Indonesia, with easy and simple requirements  and attractive features, in the context of education  and financial inclusion to encourage a culture of saving  from an early age. 10.
Saving Accountku, is a savings product for individuals with easy and light requirements issued jointly by  banks in Indonesia in order to foster a culture of saving  and improve the welfare of the community. 11.
BNI Pandai, is a savings for individuals with easy and light requirements issued by BNI which has the characteristics of a Basic Saving Account (BSA) and  can be opened through a BNI Branch Office or through  an Agent.
Time deposit  BNI Time Deposit product offers term deposit placement with a variety of currency (IDR/USD/SGD/JPY/HKD/EUR/  GBP/AUD) and attractive interest rates.
BNI Time Deposit  can be an investment choice for customers who want  relatively higher returns.
For the convenience of opening  BNI Time Deposit for customers, BNI Time Deposit  account opening services are available through the BNI  Mobile Banking application, so customers do not need to  come to conventional branch offices.
customer deposit – strategy & Productivity 2020  and Prospects & strategy 2021 customer deposit – strategy 2020  A wide selection of savings products offered by BNI  are tailored to the needs of customers at every stage  of life.
During 2020, the strategy for achieving TPF in  the consumer segment is the focus of managing the  main customer segments, Emerald and Affluent, Payroll,  merchants, and increasing customer transactions, both  debit cards and e-channels, in order to increase closed  loop transaction growth which has an impact on increasing  sustainable funds.
Taplus As the core savings product with the largest portfolio,  BNI Taplus has an important role in achieving TPF  growth.
The impact of the pandemic also made BNI to  pursue innovation through digitization on various fronts.
Various banking activities can be done through gadgets.
Starting from the need to open savings and deposits accounts which can be done through BNI Mobile Banking  by prioritizing DOA (digital opening account) services,  in addition BNI also innovates digitally by issuing BNI  Sonic (Self Service Opening Account) which can also be  accessed via EDC Android devices.
In addition, in 2020  BNI also provided loyalty programs and increase customer  transactions through the BNI POIN+ program.
bnI PoIn+ To increase customer loyalty in BNI savings products,  in 2020 BNI promoted the BNI POIN+ program.
BNI  POIN+ is a point reward program offered by BNI for all  loyal customers of BNI savings products, as a form of  appreciation for customer loyalty.
Now all financial activities  at BNI start from saving, activating e-Banking (Mobile  Banking, Internet Banking and SMS Banking), transactions  in all BNI channels (Mobile Banking, Internet Banking, SMS  Banking, ATM, Electronic Data Capture-EDC), transfers  between BNI accounts and between banks will get a  reward in the form of BNI POIN+.
The points earned by  customers will be accumulated and can be exchanged for  various attractive prizes, such as e-Vouchers at various  merchants, airplane tickets, hotels, car rental, and various  other options.
The POIN+ can also be transferred to other  BNI customers.
Customers can check and exchange points  via BNI Mobile Banking.
emerald savings In an effort to increase the funds in savings accounts in  the Emerald customer segment, BNI conducts programs  that focus on meeting customer needs and providing  more rewards to customers as a form of reward for  customer loyalty with BNI.
The programs that have been  implemented include Welcome Racing Up+ BNI Emerald  and Welcoming Package+ BNI Emerald for BNI customers  who are in priority segments, Free Trial BNI Emerald Card  for regular customers or BNI debtors, BNI Points+ Bonus  for Emerald which allows customers to earn more Points+,  as well as privilege programs with selected merchants.

The entrepreneurial segment is a target  market that is being worked on seriously by offering  BNI Taplus Bisnis to make it easier for entrepreneurs in  their  transactions with banks.

digital account opening  During 2020, especially during the PSBB & Transitional  PSBB periods that restricts the mobility of the community,  BNI provides convenience through a digital account  opening feature for BNI Taplus, BNI Taplus Muda, and  BNI Taplus Bisnis products both through the BNI Mobile  Banking application, Tokopedia platform, and other digital  account opening programs in collaboration with JD.
The advantages of this feature include  that customers do not need to come to branch offices,  do not need to videocall with bank officers, can directly  make transactions using BNI Mobile Banking, and have  the opportunity to get BNI Points+ from savings and  transaction activities.

BNI’s third party funds (TPF) is expected to grow by at  least 4-5% in 2021.
BNI continues to be committed so  that the growth of Third Party Funds continues to grow  optimally in 2021.
The strategy to increase TPF in 2021 is focused on the  Emerald, Affluent, SME (Small Medium Enterprise), payroll  and university segments, as well as the mass/upper mass  segment, through increasing closed loop transactions  and increasing e-channel transactions, both POS and e-commerce, as well as optimization of the role of BNI  Agen46.
In the Emerald segment, the strategy to increase the  savings portfolio is through new customer acquisitions  and increasing account balances by improving customer  service, providing a special BNI Emerald experience  package, rewards for customers, and other privileges.
The  development of Emerald customer service will also be  carried out by developing Emerald savings products and  developing Digital Business Wealth Management.
In the Affluent segment, the strategy to increase the savings portfolio is through the acquisition of new  customers through optimization of dataleads based on  analytical data, increasing existing customer balances  by improving customer service, providing Virtual RM &  Digital Wealth Platform services for the Affluent segment, bundling products through the synergy of BB-CR to acquire  new customers and increase the PHR (product holding  ratio).
In the SME (Small Medium Enterprise) segment, the  strategy to increase the savings portfolio is through  initiatives to position BNI as a one-stop business  solution with the acquisition of Savings as a merchant  & entrepreneurial business affiliate, increasing the  financial transactions of SME customers, merchants &  entrepreneurs through various attractive reward programs,  optimization savings as an operational account for KUR  Debtors, as well as improving Digital Personal Business  services by continuing to synergize with the Business  Banking segment, both Corporate, Medium, Small and its  subsidiaries.
The focus of payroll and universities is to make payroll  acquisitions in the Top Tier of the Regional Economic  Sector, to acquire payroll for Business Banking debtors  (Corporate, Medium & Small) as well as customers of  ministries, BUMN, BUMD, universities, hospitals, & other  educational institutions, making acquisitions Taplus Muda  Co-Brand in an educational ecosystem-based institution/ community, enhancing digital platforms for future  generations and providing convenient onboarding.
In the Mass & Upper Mass segment, the strategy to  increase the savings portfolio is through the provision  of digital onboarding & partnerships to increase the  acquisition of DOA (Digital Open Account) digital accounts  with Face Recognition, opening digital accounts through  e-commerce, digital branches, SONIC and EDC Android  as well as increasing transactions and increasing existing customer savings balances through efforts to increase  customer preferences and customer experience, education  and activation of e-channel facilities, debit usage programs  and e-channel transactions, BNI POIN+ campaigns and  POIN+ loyalty programs to BNI savings customers by  actively adding savings balances, transactions via e-channel  and debit card as well as optimization of government  assistance accounts to paid accounts.

Forex – Tom  Foreign exchange buy-sell transaction where  transaction settlement is carried out 1 (one) working  day after the date of the transaction agreement.  3.
Forex – sPoT  Foreign exchange buy-sell transaction where transaction settlement is carried out 2 (two) working  days after the date of the transaction agreement.  4.
Forex – bank notes  Transactions involving the exchange of physical ownership of the currency (banknotes) involved in the  transaction.
Distinguished	by: a.
Banking Transactions  Banknote deposits or withdrawals from customer accounts with the same currency, generating fee  income in lieu of exchange.
Trading Transactions  Buying or selling banknotes, generating revenue from the difference in exchange rates.
Investment Treasury investment products consist of Deposit on Call (DOC), Money Market Account (MMA), and retail bonds.
Details regarding investment products are described as  follows:	 1.
Placement of funds for a minimum period of 3 (three) days and up to 30 (thirty) days.
The interest rate is based on the interbank interest rates.
Can be withdrawn at any time.
Minimum placement of Rp100 million or USD75  thousand.
In the Treasury and International segment, BNI provides  investment solutions with due consideration of customer  needs and their risk types, through the offer of the best in  banking products.
The Treasury and International segment  comprises the Bank’s treasury activities including foreign  exchange transactions, money markets, capital markets  and fixed income, as well as international banking business and overseas branch supervision.
Treasury  2020 was a challenging year for BNI, especially in the Treasury segment, due to developments in the global  and domestic levels, including from the impact of the  COVID-19 pandemic.
Responding to global and domestic   economic developments, BNI Treasury segment has  implemented various strategies and policies to anticipate  existing challenges, mobilizing all available resources to  maintain  sustainable growth.
Comprehensive discussions  on segment description, strategy, productivity, and  prospects of BNI Treasury segment in 2020 are presented  as	follows: segment description  BNI treasury products are classified as transactional  products, investment products, and hedging products.
Transactional  Transactional products consist of Forex-TOD, Forex-TOM, Forex-SPOT, and Forex-Bank Notes.
Detailed description of  these	transactional	products	are	as	follow:	 1.
Forex – Tod  Foreign exchange buy-sell transaction  where the transaction agreement and transaction settlement are  carried out on the same day.
Operational Review Management   Discussion & Analysis 197 Uniting Energy to Revive the Country2020 Annual Report PT Bank Negara Indonesia (Persero) Tbk2.
money market account (mma)  a.
Placement of funds for a minimum period of 1  (one) days and up to 1 (one) year.
The interest rate is based on the interbank interest rates.
Can be withdrawn at any time.
Minimum placement of Rp1 billion or USD100  thousand. 3.
Retail bonds   Bonds are evidence of indebtedness by the issuer, which will be repaid at maturity in accordance with  the terms and conditions previously established.
Bond  transactions are made between the Treasury Division  and Individual Clients, in the following transaction  types: a.
In the primary market, for corporate bonds and  non-retail government bonds.
In the secondary market, for corporate bonds and  retail government bonds.
Non-retail government bonds and other countries’ government bonds. 4.
depo swap  A Depo Swap is an investment product in foreign  currency with a maximum rate of return and  guaranteed payment of 100% of the principal  investment placement.
Depo Swap is a combination  of forex transactions in the form of FX Swap and  deposit.
In this transaction the customers converts  their forex currency into other foreign currencies and  reconverts the forex currency in the future, at a tenor  and exchange rate established at the start of the  transaction agreement.
The foreign exchange gain on  foreign exchange transactions (forex gain) becomes the optimal return on the customers’ investment fund  placement.  5.
market linked-dual currency Investment  (ml-dcI)  ML-DCI is a structured product that is a combination  of foreign exchange savings products and FX Options.
This product provides a high return when compared to  conventional savings products as it combines savings  products linked to exchange rate movements.
This  product has non-capital protected characteristic, that  is, it does not guarantee the principal investment.
currency Forward Sale and purchase of foreign currencies where  settlement is carried out more than two business days  after the transaction date.
The exchange rate used for  forward transactions takes into account the forward  points.
•	 Domestic	Non-Deliverable	Forward	(DNDF)  A standard (plain vanilla) foreign exchange against  rupiah derivative transaction in the form of a forward  transaction with fixing mechanism conducted in the  domestic market.
A fixing mechanism is transaction  settlement mechanism with no movement of the principal funds by calculating the difference between  the forward transaction rate and the reference rate on  a certain date specified at the fixing date.
•	 PAR	Forward Par Forward is a derivative contract to make a series of  sales/purchases of one currency (reference currency)  against another currency (non-reference currency)  in a period, where the payment/delivery of funds  (settlement) is carried out more than 2 (two) working  days after the date of the transaction agreement (trade date). 2.
currency swap  ‘Buy and Sell’ or ‘Sell and Buy’ transactions in one  currency against another currency that is carried out  simultaneously with the same counterparties. 3.
currency option  Agreement to provide a right and not an obligation of  the seller (option writer) to the buyer (option holder)  to buy or sell a certain amount of nominal currency in the foreseeable future at a predetermined price (strike  price), on or before the specified time (expiry date).  4.
Interest Rate swap (IRs)  Agreement between two parties to exchange a series of fixed interest payments (fixed rate) in one currency  with a series of fluctuating interest payments (variable  rate) in the same currency (or vice versa), without the  exchange of principal loans.
•	 Overnight	Index	Swap	(OIS)  OIS is an interest rate derivative product, namely  a contract/agreement between 2 parties to  periodically exchange interest rate flows in Rupiah  during a certain contract period, calculated using  a daily interest basis (Daily Compounding).
The  transaction scheme is the same as the Interest  Rate Swap (IRS) but the method of calculating the interest is on a daily compounding basis with the  overnight benchmark interest rate.  5.
cross currency swap (ccs)  An agreement between two parties to exchange principal and interest payments in different currencies.
The exchange loan principal uses the exchange rate at  inception.  198 2020 Annual Report PT Bank Negara Indonesia (Persero) Tbk Uniting Energy to Revive the Country6.
call spread option (cso)  CSO is a structured product with a combination of  2 (two) Currency Option transactions i.
Buy Call  Option (purchase of the right to purchase a particular  currency) and Sell Call Option (sale of the right to  purchase a particular currency), for the same nominal  amount and time period, but with different strike  prices for each Buy Call Option and Sell Call Option.
The CSO transaction must be made through Dynamic  Hedging with the aim that hedging executors are not  exposed to exchange rate risk due to market rates  beyond the Sell Call Option strike price.
•	 Series	Of	Call	Spread  Series of CSOs is a contract for a series of call  spread option within a certain period.
Treasury segment strategy 2020  During 2020, BNI implemented the following strategies  and	policies	in	the	Treasury	segment: 1.
Manage short-term liquidity through the issuance  of Negotiable Certificates of Deposit (NCD), use  of assets held as underlying, such as Bankers  Acceptance and Term Repo as well as f Bank  Indonesia facilities such as GWM averaging, and  others. 2.
Actively manage the Marketable Securities portfolio with measurable risks, both as a liquid tool and as  an activity that generates Capital Gain, by taking  advantage of market momentum and in line with the  direction of interest rate movements.  3.
Optimize the pricing policy, both in terms of assets as well as liabilities to reduce pressure on business  margins. 4.
Develop digital applications for Treasury products and services, such as BNI Digihedge, which is an expert system with artificial intelligence that can help  customers identify their need for hedging. 5.
Optimize the business potential of debtors through synergies with business units and subsidiaries in line  with the close loop transaction program.6.
Increase the competence and capacity of RM and marketers so that they are able to provide the best  Treasury solutions to meet customers’ business  needs.

International banking domestic services  The International banking segment offers business services from branch offices in Indonesia (domestic), including banking  products in the form of BNI Smart Trade, Financial Institutions, Remittances and International Desks. 200 2020 Annual Report PT Bank Negara Indonesia (Persero) Tbk Uniting Energy to Revive the CountrybnI smart Trade  BNI Smart Trade consists of trade products, trade services, and trade financing.
Trade Product doc collectionGuaranteeskbdnletter of creditTrade service settlementRealizationadvisingIssuanceTrade Financing bills PaymentRefinancingdiscountingnegotiationbnI smartTrade 5.
Irrevocable and confirmed l/c  This form of L/C is considered the most perfect and  safest from the point of view of the L/C recipient  (beneficiary), as the payment or settlement of draft  drawn on this L/C is fully guaranteed by the opening  bank or by the advising bank, if all conditions are met,  and not easily undone due to its irrevocable nature.
Trade services  Trade Services is a trade business that provides services to customers to obtain services in the context of trading  or trade transactions of export/import as well as domestic  scope.
The	following	are	trade	services: 1.
Issuance  Issuance is a service for issuing an instrument (L/C,  Domestic L/C, Guarantee) that guarantees payment  certainty or guarantees the implementation of  certain contracts to the recipient with conditions in  accordance with the terms of L/C, Domestic L/C, or  Guarantee.  2.
advising  Advising is a service to forward L/C, Domestic L/C, or Guarantee to be delivered to the recipient/beneficiary  in accordance with the instructions from the Issuing  Bank.
Trade Product 1.
letter of credit  Letter of Credit is a guarantee of payment instrument  issued by the bank (Issuing Bank) to recipients  (Beneficiary) which is subject to Uniform Customs and  Practice for Documentary Credits (UCP). 2.
domestic letter of credit   A Domestic Letter of Credit is a guarantee of payment instrument issued by the bank (Issuing Bank) to  recipients (Beneficiary), which is subject to Bank  Indonesia Regulations and is used for domestic trade  transactions.  3.
demand Guarantee/standby letter of credit  (Guarantee)  A Guarantee is an agreement/letter issued by the  issuing bank that is obligated to pay to the guarantee  beneficiary party (Beneficiary) when the secured party  (Applicant) is in breach of contract or default.
The  Guarantee issued in the form of Demand Guarantee  is subject to Uniform Rules for Demand Guarantee  (URDG) or Standby Letter of Credit subject to UCPDC  or International Standby Practices (ISP).  4.
documentary collection (non lc)  Documentary Collection is a payment system for world trade conducted through banking services in the  form of undocumented bills subject to Uniform Rules  for Collections (URC).
Operational Review Management   Discussion & Analysis 201 Uniting Energy to Revive the Country2020 Annual Report PT Bank Negara Indonesia (Persero) Tbk3.
Realization  Realization is a service for delivering documents in  the framework of trade to the document recipient as  importer/buyer with agreed conditions.  4.
settlement  Settlement (Payment) is a service for settling trade  transactions in the form of payments for transactions  that have been executed or agreed upon.
This service  is a cycle of trade transactions by making payments to  exporters/sellers via bank transfer.
Trade Financing Trade Financing is a business managed by the International  Division to provide financing to customers in the context  of trade/trade transactions with instruments in the form of  L/C, Domestic L/C, Documentary Collection, Bills Payment,  and Invoice or bill-based.
The	following	are	trade	financing	services: 1.
negotiation  Negotiation is the takeover of the payment of draft  drawn by the beneficiary to a bank based on the  document presented and stated in accordance with  the terms and conditions of L/C/Domestic L/C/SBLC  with a tenor of sight. 2.
discounting  Discounting is the takeover of the payment of draft  value drawn by the beneficiary to a bank based on the  document presented and stated in accordance with  the terms and conditions of L/C/Domestic L/C/SBLC  with tenor usage. 3.
Refinancing  Refinancing is financing in the form of taking over  payments against the background of L/C or Domestic  L/C issuance transactions.
Financing in the form of  refinancing can be carried out at the beginning of the  issuance or when the payment is nearing maturity. 4.
non l/c Financing  Non L/C Financing is financing to exporters/sellers  and importers/buyers on the basis of documentary  collection/open account transactions.
bnI Trade online BNI Trade Online is a trade transaction service for  customers using a web-based application system, which  can be used by customers to apply online for trade  transactions or receive the results of trade transaction  decisions from the bank.
Financial Institution Products and services  Products and services in the Financial Institution business  are	Business	to	Business	(B2B)	services	as	follow: 1.
bank Guarantee under counter (bGuc)   The issuance of Bank Guarantees based of request and with a sure guarantee from the correspondent  bank (The Instructing Party).  2.
bank to bank Financing – Refinancing  A financing facility made by BNI to a correspondent  bank in the form of payment for the realization of LC  or Domestic LCN based on a loan agreement between  BNI and the  correspondent bank  3.
bank to bank Financing-Trade advance  Financing  It is a financing made by BNI to correspondent banks with underlying transactions in the form of LC/ Domestic LC and non-LC/Domestic LC. 4.
bank to bank Financing-Forfaiting  Purchasing the right to collect Banker’s Acceptances  (B/As) held by the Correspondent Bank as a  Nominated Bank (forfaitee) in respect of L/C or  Domestic L/C transactions without recourse. 5.
bank to bank Financing-Term loan Facility bank  Granting of credit facilities to other banks either with the status of BUMN, BUSN, BUMD, or Branch Offices  of Foreign Banks domiciled in Indonesia. 6.
Risk Partication  Is the partial transfer of risk owned by an applicant  bank to BNI in a funded or unfunded form that is  related to trade transactions agreed upon between the  applicant bank and other banks.
Remittance services Remittance is a form of money transfer service to another designated party (beneficiary customer or institution) based  on a written order or request from an individual, legal  entity (ordering customer or institution) to remitting bank/ institution both inside and outside country. 202 2020 Annual Report PT Bank Negara Indonesia (Persero) Tbk Uniting Energy to Revive the CountryThe	types	of	Remittance	services	are	as	follow: 1.
Incoming Fund Transfer or Incoming transfer (ITR) or  Incoming remittances Remittances from individuals  or legal entities through overseas remitting banks in  foreign currency/rupiah, or through domestic banks,  especially for foreign currency, addressed to BNI  as the recipient bank, for recipients’ benefit whose  names are designated in the remittance, either as  BNI customers or non-customers in the country.
The  ITR transaction code in BNI is S06.
BNI Wesel PIN  is a Remittance/Incoming Transfer (ITR) service from  overseas, that can be exchanged for cash (without  an account) in BNI outlets and BNI paying agents  such as Pos Indonesia, Alfamart, and pawnshops.
Disbursements are made through a correct PIN  number and valid identity cards (KTP/SIM/ Passport).  2.
Outgoing Fund Transfer (OTR) or Outgoing remittances Unconditional written order from BNI at the request of a customer and/or for BNI’s benefit  addressed to the correspondent bank to pay a  certain amount of money to a specified person/entity  (beneficiary).
Includes foreign currency remittances to  correspondent banks at home and abroad.
The OTR  BNI transaction code is S10.
BNI remittances can be  received on the same day (same day service) with  time limits (cut off time) determined by each currency.
BNI also has multi currency remittances services that  can be received in 125 (one hundred twenty five)  types of local currency from 160 (one hundred sixty)  countries.
International desk As a Gate to Investment, BNI focuses on increasing the  role of Overseas Branch Offices and Financial Institutions  (FI) in supporting Foreign Direct Investment (FDI), as well  as developing an International Desk in providing banking  services to foreign entities investing in Indonesia through  the	following	facilities:	 1.
loan  The International Desk unit provides loan facilities in the form of IDR-denominated loans or offshore loans  in USD and JPY currencies as well as Open Account  Financing (OAF) for international corporate clients  in Indonesia with competitive interest rates, based  on Stand by LC (SBLC)  guaranteed by international  banking/financial institutions.
In providing these  loans or Open Account Financing (OAF) scheme, the  International Desk coordinates with the Credit unit. 2.
Third Party Funds   Cooperating with branches in providing Savings,  Current and Time Deposit account opening services to  customers, both foreign individuals and international  corporations in Indonesia. 3.
cash management  Cooperating with the Transaction Banking Services (TBS) division in the marketing of BNI Cash  management products to international corporation  customers in Indonesia.  4.
credit card   Cooperating with the Card Business (BSK) division in offering personalized  credit card to foreign individuals  and international corporations.
overseas branch office (kcln) The Overseas Branch Office (KCLN) network provides BNI  with a  competitive edge in strengthening its International  business and to support global business partners in  expanding their business.
In implementing its business, KCLN applies 3 Strategic  Values	as	follows: 1.
source of International Funding  BNI focuses on increasing the role of Overseas Branch  Office (KCLN) and correspondent banks as a source  of low-cost funding to support BNI’s business growth  and customer business development, especially  export-based corporations. 2.
Go Global with bnI  BNI strives to support Indonesian businesses to expand in the global market and play an active role in  providing digital-based global services. 3.
Gate to Investment  Optimizing the role of Overseas Branch Office and  Financial Institution (FI) units to support foreign  investment as well as optimizing the International  Desk in providing banking and advisory services to  foreign entities interested in investing in Indonesia.
Products and services Provided by overseas branch  office (kcln) The above-mentioned strategic values are manifested in  the form of products and services provided by the KCLN to  the	customers,	including: Operational Review Management   Discussion & Analysis 203 Uniting Energy to Revive the Country2020 Annual Report PT Bank Negara Indonesia (Persero) Tbklending Products  The provision of lending products is focused on the value- chain of Indonesia-related companies to assist in their  business	development	through: 1.
local loan   Local loan is a credit facility offered by Overseas  Branch Office (KCLN) to Indonesian business groups  or the  overseas counter parties of Indonesian  companies, both bilaterally and syndicated.
The types  of loans offered can be in the form of Working Capital  Loans, Investment Loans and term loans.  2.
offshore loan   Offshore loan is a facility provided by the Overseas  Branch Office (KCLN) to debtor customers in  Indonesia in the form of a foreign currency- denominated working capital loan (short-term)  to finance the procurement of capital goods for  the purpose of rehabilitation, modernization, and expansion, with medium or long-term loan settlement. 3.
Trade loan   Trade Loan Is a financing facility offered by the Overseas Branch Offices (KCLN),  based on Trade  Finance transactions conducted by Indonesian  business groups and the overseas counter parties of  Indonesian companies.
Third Party Fund Products  Overseas Branch Offices with Full License Bank status  (KCLN Singapore, KCLN Hong Kong, KCLN Tokyo and  KCLN Seoul) can carry out activities to collect Third Party Funds (DPK) from local customers where the KCLN is located, consisting of Savings, Time Deposits, and Current  Account	products.

savings  Savings account developed to accommodate individual  customer needs. 2.
current accounts  Deposit service for individual and corporate customers  to meet their payment needs for operational activities  with check as a means of withdrawal. 3.
deposits Time deposit services offered by KCLN with tenor  ranging from 1 (one) to 12 (twelve) months.
bank to bank Funding Bank to Bank Funding is an interbank lending-borrowing  activity to meet liquidity and financing needs for  customers.
These activities include, among others, Banker  Acceptance, Term Loans or Money Market Borrowing.
Bank to Bank Funding is carried out by leveraging on  synergies and mutual business relationships with leading  correspondent banks around the world.

International segment strategy in 2020 The International division, through its vision of becoming a major player in the international trade and international  payment business for the banking industry in Indonesia,  continues to support BNI’s business through the  implementation of various strategies during 2020.
The entire KCLN network is located in business and  economic centers of the world, such as in Singapore, Hong  Kong, Tokyo, Seoul, London and New York, as well as 1  (one) Representative Office in Yangon representing the  Indochina region.
One of the keys to the success of the international  segment is to focus and be selective in managing assets  by	controlling	business	risk	through,	among	others: 1.
Focus on Indonesia Related businesses, particularly in  supporting the Value Chain of Indonesian companies’  businesses abroad and providing superior global services on a digital basis.
This business focus has  succeeded in improving; a.
Supervision of business activities.
Domestic trade business growth.
Encouraging expansion of local loans at each  KCLN.
The delay in investing in the oil and gas sector has affected the international business, which is reflected in the  decrease in transactions of Bank Guarantees issued on the  basis of guarantees from banks abroad.
Apart from the decline in the Financial Institution business,  the remittance business was also affected by the Covid-19  pandemic.
Revenues from the Remittance business  decreased by 7.6% compared to 2019, however, if  seen from the perspective of the number of remittance  transaction slips, it tends to be stable (decreased by 0.36%  compared to last year).
This condition is supported by  strategies implemented during the Covid-19 pandemic, including:	 •	 Focus	on	Indonesian	Migrant	Workers	(PMI)	as	the	 largest contributor to remittance transaction slips.
In addition to income/fees from PMI remittance  transactions, BNI also succeeded in improving the  performance of opening PMI savings accounts by  41% and PMI’s Third Party Funds (DPK) by 36%,  compared to the achievements at the end of 2019.
•	 Significant	growth	in	transactions	from	countries	 implementing digital transactions, including South  Korea, Taiwan and Singapore.
Among a number of digital breakthroughs by BNI were  the addition of the International Remittance feature to BNI  Mobile Banking, increased utilization of BNI MoRe (Mobile  Remittance) in Singapore, and increased remittance  cooperation with mobile apps partners in South Korea and Taiwan.
This is very helpful for customer remittance  transactions, especially during the Covid-19 pandemic  where customers do not need to come to BNI outlets  or BNI remittance partners to conduct  money transfer  transactions.
Amid the slowing pace of global and domestic economic  growth, the International Desk business and the Trade  Finance business were still able to record positive  performance and growth.
This is reflected in the growth of  third party funds and loans disbursed by the International  Desk which has increased quite rapidly.
On a yoy basis,  third party funds managed by the International Desk  experienced a growth of 25.6%, while loans disbursement  grew by 33.2% (yoy).
This growth contributed to the  increase in income received in the form of interest income  and fee income, which grew by 45.8% compared to 2019.
This performance was the contribution of the International  Desk, formerly known as the Japan Desk, established  by  BNI since 2012.
The Japan Desk has collaborated with  54 Japan Regional Banks (JRB) through the placement of  JRB trainees at BNI,  to help provide referrals for affiliated  companies in Indonesia where their parent company in  Japan has become a customer or debtor of the JRB.  206 2020 Annual Report PT Bank Negara Indonesia (Persero) Tbk Uniting Energy to Revive the Country2.
Take advantage of the trend of low interest rates on  world financial markets to increase customer business  competitiveness and optimize Net Interest Income; 3.

aTm Banking service channel, which is  ready to facilitate customers for 24 hours in making cash deposit-withdrawal transactions (Cash Recycle Machine), balance checks, transfers, payments and purchases.

sms banking BNI SMS Banking is a banking service facility that can be used by customers to transact transfers, payments and purchases which can be accessed through the BNI SMS Banking application (for smartphone users based on Android & iOS), Syntax SMS and access to USSD * 141 #.
mobile banking BNI Mobile Banking makes it easy for individual customers to make transfers, investments and bill payments in one application.
BNI Mobile Banking is available on IOS and Android devices and can be activated  and used for overseas transactions.
BNI Mobile Banking has also been equipped with reliable features that facilitate customer transactions, such as Mobile Cash, Biometric Login, User-ID Autofilling, account opening and credit card and loan applications. 208 Satukan Energi untuk Kebangkitan Negeri2020 annual Report PT Bank Negara Indonesia (Persero) Tbk 209 Uniting Energy to Revive the Country2020 Annual Report PT Bank Negara Indonesia (Persero) Tbk Internet banking BNI Internet Banking is a banking  service channel that can be accessed through the BNI Internet Banking URL, either via a computer or smartphone.
BNI Internet Banking also has a flagship feature in the form of Personal Financial Management that allows customers to make financial plans according to their  needs complete with automatic  deposit scheduling, and can be used to monitor cash flow and trends in spending/inflows of funds in graphical form.
BNI Internet Banking is also equipped with security standards that use two types of financial transaction authorization tools, namely BNI e-Secure and BNI m-Secure according to customer needs in conducting business transactions.
agen46 Agen46 is a partner of BNI in providing banking services to the public in the context of financial inclusion.
In addition to BNI partners in providing various kinds of banking services, Agen46 also has various government programs, such as the distribution of social assistance and subsidies, both cash and non-cash.
Through Agen46,  banking transactions are easier, faster  and more accessible to the local community.
sms notification It is an information service on banking transactions carried out by customers which is sent via SMS to the mobile number registered by the customer for notification of debit/credit transactions made by customers, especially BNI Taplus/BNI Giro IDR Individual account holders.
Tapcash TapCash is card-based electronic money (chip-based) in lieu of cash that can be transacted at various acceptance points in the form of BNI cooperating merchants as well as various modes of transportation,  parking and toll roads.
TapCash users  are also spoiled with the TapCash Go application which makes it easy to check balances and top up their TapCash cards.
In increasing the ease with which customers can obtain and top up their TapCash cards, BNI has expanded its cooperation with various retailer, e-commerce, partners & fintek partners.
iPay BNI iPay is a product derivative of BNI Internet Banking that makes it easy for BNI Internet Banking users to complete online shopping transactions in one transaction flow.
After selecting goods or services on the e-commerce site, the User will be directed to the BNI iPay site to be able to make immediate payments using the user id, password and secure  code generated by e-secure or m-secure  BNI Internet Banking.
smartpay BNI Smartpay is a product derivative of BNI SMS Banking that provides seamless transactions for customers using BNI SMS Banking in their online shopping transactions in one transaction flow.
After selecting goods  or services on an e-commerce site, the  next customer only needs to enter the challenge pin from the incoming SMS 3346.
edc bnI The BNI EDC merchant network is a network that serves payment transactions using APMK (credit, debit and prepaid cards).
The BNI EDC merchant network has wide acceptance, which is a collaboration between BNI as the acquirer bank and the principal, both global principals such as VISA, MasterCard, JCB, UPI, and local  principal.

As one of the largest banks in Indonesia, the role of  BNI and its subsidiaries in the BNI Group in the financial  industry has occupied a very strategic position.
Therefore,  BNI continues to improve the synergy between BNI and its  subsidiaries so that it can provide comprehensive financial  services as a team to customers.
Following the applicable regulations in the banking industry,  BNI manages its subsidiary companies by investing in  companies engaged in the financial sector.
As of the end  of 2020, BNI had equity investments in 9 subsidiaries.
The majority ownership in several subsidiaries is aimed at  building a strategic partnership and synergies to provide  added value for BNI customers.
Meanwhile, minority  ownership is carried out to comply with applicable policies/ regulations such as the provisions of OJK and BI, as well  as in building business cooperation with BNI partners.
BNI’s Subsidiaries are PT Bank BNI Syariah (99.94%), PT  BNI Life Insurance (60.0%), PT BNI Securities (75.0%),  PT BNI Multifinance (99.9 %), and BNI Remittance Ltd  (100.0%).
The development of the increasingly diverse needs of the public and corporations for financial services requires banks to provide integrated financial services.
With the  existence of limits on banking services/products from  the authorities, banks are unable to fulfill all stakeholder  needs for financial services, so it is necessary to involve  subsidiary companies. 216 2020 Annual Report PT Bank Negara Indonesia (Persero) Tbk Uniting Energy to Revive the CountryPeRFoRmance oF bnI subsIdIaRIes subsidiariesGrowth 2020 2020 2019 2018 2017 2016 Rp million % Rp billion Rp billion Rp billion Rp billion Rp billion  BNI Syariah -97.80 -16.21% 505.35 603.15 416.08 306.69 277.37  BNI Life -148.78 -49.25% 153.32 302.10 185.04 374.90 183.95  BNI Sekuritas 15.00 72.41% 35.72 20.72 18.28 10.91 12.34  BNI Multifinance -1.47 -7.61%  17.90 19.37 27.36 26.87 7.41 BNI Remittance 3.32 429.23% 4.09 0.77 0.37 -1.00 0.21 Total -229.73 -24.28% 716.38  946.12  647.13  718.37 481.28 Looking ahead, BNI has several business development strategies to improve financial performance, business growth,  customer	satisfaction,	and	the	position	of	subsidiaries	among	peer	groups	and	industry	in	2021	as	follows: •	 Increase	the	synergy	of	the	BNI	Group.

PT bnI sekuritas (bnI sekuritas) Productivity, Income, and Profitability At the end of 2020, BNI Sekuritas managed to book a net profit of Rp36 billion, growing by 72.41% from Rp21 billion in 2019, reaching 75.01% of the target of Rp48 billion.
Operating income in 2020 of Rp329 billion grew by 13.82% from 2019  amounting to Rp289 billion.
The main source of income mainly came from brokerage commissions with a contribution of  Rp122 billion or 37.18% of the total operating income of BNI Sekuritas, investment management fees (through BNI Asset  Management as a subsidiary of BNI Sekuritas) of Rp96 billion or 29.39%, and Investment Banking Fee of Rp47 billion or  14.16%.
The total value of BNI Sekuritas equity brokerage transactions in 2020 was Rp 89 trillion, an increase of 6% from  2019 amounting to Rp83.7 trillion.
Online transaction value contributed Rp 63.5 trillion, while the total value of Regular  transactions was Rp 25.5 trillion.
The number of active BNI Sekuritas accounts in 2020 was recorded at 144,802 accounts,  an increase of 45% from 2019 of 99,954 accounts.

PT bnI multifinance (bnI multifinance) Productivity, Income, and Profitability As of December 2020, BNI Multifinance posted positive performance with a net profit of Rp18 billion, a decrease of 7.61%  from 2019 of Rp19 billion, reaching 51.4% of the target at the end of 2020 of Rp35 billion.
Assets reached Rp1,615 billion,  decreased by 12.05% from 2019 amounting to Rp1,837 billion, and reached 100% of the end-of-2020 target of Rp1,616  billion.
The performance of BNI Multifinance in 2020 focused on investment (commercial) financing in the form of commercial  vehicles, heavy equipment, etc.
for BNI referral (new) customers, BNI Multifinance Repeats-Order (RO) customers, and Car- Lease financing through the Car Ownership Program (COP) for the segment of government officials, corporate employees  as well as employees of the BNI Business Group, as well as Car Rent to BNI and the Group.
The company carries out multi- financing (multi-product & BNIMF OTO) by focusing on BNI and BNI Group employees and has also started AR financing  with a focus on customer-selected flow risk to maintain a healthy portfolio.

Total BNI Remittance assets in 2020 amounted to 11,804 million, reaching 299.89% of the 2020 target Rp 3,936 million.
Total remittance transactions during 2020 were recorded at 270.7 thousand slips or decreased by 41% compared to the  previous year of 303.4 thousand slips.
The decrease in transactions was more due to changes in customer transaction  patterns who began to switch to using BNI Mobile Banking where there was a significant increase in the number of PMIs  opening accounts in 2020 with an average monthly account opening of 1,200 accounts and 80% of them activated BNI.
Transactions using BNI Mobile Banking were an option during the Covid-19 pandemic, where the Hong  Kong government issued a ban on gathering regulations so that many PMIs prefer transactions from their respective  homes.
The 2020 performance was achieved by improving remittance services and opening BNI Taplus PMI accounts 2020.
The  expansion of the remittance network was carried out by strengthening the cooperation that has been established between  BNI and local Money Service Operators (MSO) which have wider network outlets.
With this collaboration, BNI remittance  services can be felt more evenly throughout Hong Kong.
Collaborations have been established with 5 local MSOs, namely  BEST Remittance, Uniforex, Fast Access Corporation Ltd.
, and Nice Star Corporation Ltd.
During 2020, BNI Remittance is also active in organizing various educational-based marketing programs, including a savings  balance improvement program, an ATM and Mobile Banking utilization increase program, and a customer gets customer  program through the digital BNI account opening application (E-Form).
Through the WE program with BNI, BNI Remittance actively initiates a capacity-building program for PMI in Hong Kong.
The enthusiasm of PMI to increase capacity, as well as to widen networks among migrant workers, banks and other related  parties can be seen from the large number of participants who attend each training held.
The training is carried out in two  stages, namely soft skills training in the form of entrepreneurial seminars and hard skills training in the form of skills practice  classes.
In 2020, this capacity-building program will be further strengthened by involving communities, one of which is the  Nahdlatul Ulama Hong Kong community, which is through the cooperation in issuing Hong Kong NU Membership Cards  based on BNI Debit Cards.
