It is also supported by the changes  in people’s behavior that demand convenience and  speed across all transaction activities, from consumer to  corporate level.
This shifting behavior has paved the way  for digital transactions, such as account opening, which  initially required customers to directly visit the branch, but  now this activity can be performed from the palm of their  hands through their own gadgets, anywhere and anytime, so that customers can do more important things in their lives.
This is in line with the BNI brand communication in  2019, namely, Be BNI, Be Exponential, in which all of  the convenience and comprehensiveness that BNI digital  services bring, will provide an advantage in customers’  lives such as having more time for family, relatives or self- development.
Competition in the banking business today happens  not only among banks, but also with technology-based  financial business (Fintech), urging BNI to maintain  its competitiveness under the rapidly growing market  development and needs.
Management   Discussion & Analysis 229 Uniting Energy to Revive the Country2020 Annual Report PT Bank Negara Indonesia (Persero) TbkBNI as a financial institution  that provides banking services is committed to providing ease of  transactions in this condition  by providing digital-based services, one of which is through BNI Mobile Banking.
As a financial service institution, BNI is committed to  providing ease of transactions during these unprecedented  circumstances by offering digital-based services; one  of which is through BNI Mobile Banking.
BNI Mobile  Banking is a solution for customers to carry out financial  transactions without having to leave the house.
Simply  by using a smartphone, customers can carry out banking  transactions, ranging from paying bills to investing.
This  convenience has made BNI Mobile Banking a digital  financial platform that excels in services.
maRkeTInG sTRa TeGy Achieving the business target throughout 2020 amidst the Covid-19 pandemic was a tremendous challenge for  BNI Sales Team in marketing BNI products.
In the midst  of conditions that limited direct or face to face sales &  marketing activities, several strategies were implemented  by the marketing team to adapt to these conditions,  including: •	 Adjusting	marketing	strategies	by	exploring	potential	 leads from BNI internal data.
•	 Carrying	out	greeting,	delivering	market	updates	and	 product offerings through WA Blast.
Sales team also educated customers on digital transactions through  Mobile Banking, SMS Banking and Internet banking,  delivered through WA Blast.
•	 Conducting	digital-based	sales	activities.
Several	sales	 activities involving digital tools include, among others,  the Digital Opening Account for opening a saving  account, Digi Loan for the acquisition of consumer credit products, and the use of online application or  e-Form to facilitate Consumer Credit application.
•	 Optimizing	partnership	with	fintech	and	e-commerce	 as sales channel, such as Paylater-Traveloka, DUMI- FIDAC, Tokopedia, etc.
•	 Conducting	digital	sales	events,	including	holding	a	 virtual housing expo, namely BNI Griya Online Expo  in July 2020 and the Asia Virtual Property Expo in  November 2020, in which BNI cooperates with an  e-commerce company in the property sector called  Rumah.
In 2020, BNI’s commitment to remain consistent as a  Digital Financial Institution underwent a test.
On March  2, 2020, the first case of Covid-19 in Indonesia was  announced by President Joko Widodo himself.
As a follow-up, the government decided to impose PSBB  (Large-Scale Social Restrictions) in almost all cities in  Indonesia with the aim of preventing the Covid-19 virus  from spreading out.
This policy required people to perform  many activities from home, such as school, prayer, and  working.
The concept of social distancing was believed to be the effective way to mitigate the spread of this virus. 230 2020 Annual Report PT Bank Negara Indonesia (Persero) Tbk Uniting Energy to Revive the Country•	 Hosting	online	gatherings	with	developer	partners	 to maintain relationship with customers during the  pandemic.
•	 Enhancing	the	capabilities	of	the	BNI	Marketer	Team	 by providing selling skills training virtually.
In order to maximize the results from marketing aspects,  the marketing activities were focused on the wider  community through several digital platforms that have  been widely used by BNI.
One of them was the use  of BNI’s own organic social media, especially because  as of December 19, 2020, BNI’s social media accounts  already had 1,236,946 followers on Twitter account @ BNI; 370,725 followers on Instagram @bni46; and 362,567  fans on Facebook page ‘BNI’.
The engagement rate on  these three organic social media of BNI was one of the  best in the banking business sector.
Public enthusiasm  for some of the new features of digital financial services abovementioned has received a very good response, as  can be seen from the numerous testimonies shared across  BNI social media accounts.
Marketing activities were also carried out through paid  placements on social media or by using online publishers  such as placements on Detik.
com, Tribunnews.
com and many more.
The selection of publisher  was based on the achievement obtained by the publisher,  especially those within the top 1-5 rank in monthly visitors.
This activity was also carried out with the intention of  expanding the scope of the message to be conveyed.
Apart from digital media, other platforms that were also  exploited to promote these features were offline media  such as through adlibs on Radio, ads on television,  billboard installation, advertising in print media and others.
In marketing digital products and services during this  PSBB period, especially for BNI Mobile Banking, BNI also  adapted by implementing a communication strategy based  on empathy and sympathy.
It can be seen from BNI’s  initiatives, namely the #AntarkanSemangat Movement.
#AntarkanSemangat was a social movement that  aimed to provide a positive spirit and optimism called  #AntarkanSemangat.
This movement involved all BNI  employees, commonly referred to as BNI Hi-Movers,  as well as general public who wanted to show their  empathy, especially to medical workers.
It was carried out  by donating various needs of medical devices, groceries,  and food as a form of support for the medical workers.
This movement was amplified through social media  and produced a very good result, with a total of 16,594  hashtags on Instagram and Twitter, and hit 347,035,367  impressions.
BNI also proved its success in adapting to existing conditions.
During this pandemic, BNI reformatted events  that were usually held offline to be conducted online.
Various kinds of online events have been successfully  held throughout 2020, from Music Performances to  Conferences.
The initial activity held was a Virtual Concert entitled  ‘Konser Satukan Energi untuk Indonesia’ (United Energy  for Indonesia Concert) in commemoration of BNI’s  74th Anniversary.
This concert was one of a series of  communications strategies carried out by BNI to promote  public optimism through specially curated songs.
At this  concert, BNI collaborated with Erwin Gutawa Orchestra  as the music arranger and with singers from various  generations ranging from Ardhito Pramono, Yura Yunita,  Tulus and others.
This event managed to attract great  attention, with the number of viewers reaching 456,541 people.
In celebrating the 75th Anniversary of Republic of  Indonesia, BNI collaborated with Erwin Gutawa Orchestra  by inviting the Weird Genius music group that has brought  an international conversation as well as other talented  young musicians such as Andmesh Kamaleng and Isyana  Sarasvati under an event titled ‘Pentas Musik Satukan  Energi Untuk Indonesia Maju’ (United Energy for Advanced  Indonesia Musical Performance).
In this occasion, BNI also  presented a special performance from Daniel Mananta  who brought key messages that Indonesian people would  always come together to move forward and rise again.
This  activity was also considered to be successful in attracting  public’s attention, reaching 1,310,303 viewers.
Not only an online event of concerts, to celebrate 2020  Youth Pledge Day, BNI held the #GaPakeNanti Generation  Conference	to	mobilize	Indonesian	youth	to	become: •	 Proactive •	 Be	aware	of	the	importance	of	health •	 Resilient	in	all	conditions,	and •	 Highly	Motivated.
The conference was divided into 4 sessions, in which BNI  invited aspiring young speakers for each session.
The  speakers are successful figure in their respective fields,  such as Chelsea Islan, Rizky Febian, Kemal Pahlevi, Putri  Tanjung, Prita Ghozie, Daniel Wenas and many more.
This  event received another warm welcome, participated by  1,311,644 viewers when the event took place.

The Financial  Statements was audited by the Public Accounting Firm  of Purwantono, Sungkoro & Surja (Ernst & Young) and  received a fair  opinion, in all material aspects, for the  presentation of the consolidated financial position of PT  Bank Negara Indonesia (Persero) Tbk and its subsidiaries  as of December 31, 2020, as well as the consolidated  financial results and cash flows for the year ending on that  date, in accordance with Financial Accounting Standards in  Indonesia.
The independent auditors report to shareholders  is dated January 22, 2021, and signed by Muhammad  Kurniawan with public accountant license No.

In 2020, BNI recorded a  moderate 5.4% growth of total assets in line with the slower growth of assets in the national  banking sector, as the domestic  economy declined due to the impact of the Covid-19 pandemic during the year.
Management   Discussion & Analysis 237 Uniting Energy to Revive the Country2020 Annual Report PT Bank Negara Indonesia (Persero) Tbk Unless stated otherwise, the values of accounts specified within this report represent net value after deduction of  allowance for impairment losses.
STATEMENTS OF FINANCIAL POSITION Assets In 2020, BNI recorded a moderate 5.4% growth of total assets in line with the slower growth of assets in the national  banking sector, as the domestic economy declined due to the impact of the COVID-19 pandemic during the year.
The  moderate growth in total assets mainly reflects the increase in loan outstanding (gross) by 5.3%, or higher than average  industry growth, from Rp556.8 trillion in 2019 to Rp586.2 trillion the following year.
Net loan outstanding grew by 0.4%  from Rp539.9 trillion to Rp542.0 trillion at the end of 2020.
The low growth of net loan outstanding reflects the additional  provision for loan impairment expected on the implementation of SFAS 71 in the amount of Rp12.9 trillion after taking into  account deferred taxes.
In line with BNI’s core business in loan disbursement, the loan outstanding account contributed  the bulk of total assets at 60.8% in 2020, compared with 63.8% in the previous year.
Other earning assets in the form of  government bonds contributed 10.2% to BNI’s total assets, and showed an increase of 11.9% from Rp81.0 trillion in 2019  to Rp90.7 trillion in 2020.

BNI posted Rp35.1 trillion in current accounts with Bank Indonesia in 2020.
This amount represents a decline of 5.5%  from the corresponding position a year earlier at Rp37.1 trillion.
Current accounts with Bank Indonesia represents 3.9%  of total assets in 2020, down from 4.4% the previous year.
BNI’s Legal Reserve Requirement (LRR) has complied with  the provisions of Bank Indonesia Regulation (PBI) No.15/15/PBI/2013 dated December 24, 2013 on Commercial Bank  Legal Reserve Requirement denominated in Rupiah and Foreign Currencies for Conventional Banks, as was amended on  a number of occasions, the latest of which is by Regulation of Members of the Board of Governors (PADG) No. 22/10/ PADG/2020 effective as of May 1, 2020.

Bills and Other Receivables  BNI posted Rp17.9 trillion of bills and other receivables in  2020, representing a decline of 6.8%.
The decline mainly  reflects the decline in rupiah-denominated open account  financing to Rp11.8 trillion in 2020 from Rp14.0 trillion the  previous year.
Rupiah-denominated bills and other receivables accounted  for the largest portion at 73.4% and 83.2% respectively  of total bills and other receivables in 2020 and 2019.
Bills  and other receivables are in the form of Domestic Letter of  Credit (SKBDN) and bills, as well as other receivables from  open account financing and supply chain financing.
Acceptance Receivables Based on the recipient, BNI’s acceptance receivables is distinguished to non-bank and bank borrowers.
BNI’s  acceptance receivables amounts to Rp20.6 trillion in 2020,  up by 10.9% from the previous period at Rp18.6 trillion.
The increase is mainly attributed to rupiah-denominated  acceptance receivables to customers of the Bank that  amounted to Rp16.2 trillion in 2020, compared to Rp13.2  trillion in the previous year.
Based on Bank Indonesia’s collectibility classification,  an outstanding amount of Rp18.7 trillion is classified as  current with the remaining Rp2.0 trillion classified as  special mention, with allowance for impairment losses  formed in accordance with the prevailing provisions.
Management believes that the amount of allowance for  impairment losses formed is sufficient.
Derivative Receivables In the normal course of business, BNI enters into  transactions involving derivative financial instruments such  as foreign currency forward contracts, foreign currency  swaps, interest rate swaps and spot transactions for  financing, trading and hedging purposes.
The instrument  that BNI uses is classified based on the type of risk  associated with exchange rate, interest rate and both.
Derivative receivables that are based on exchange rate are  in the form of buy/sell forward contracts, buy/sell currency  swaps, buy/sell currency spot, and buy/sell currency  options.
Interest rate related instruments comprise of  interest rate swaps while exchange and interest rate  related instruments are in the form of USD cross currency  and interest rate swaps.
On a cumulative basis, BNI’s derivative receivables is  valued at Rp1.5 trillion in 2020, representing a significant  increase of 367.7% from the amount recorded a year earlier of Rp312 billion.
Of the total derivative receivables,  US Dollar-denominated sell currency swaps accounted for  a dominant portion at Rp1.3 trillion in 2020, compared with  Rp245.1 billion the year previously.
All of the derivative  receivables as of December 31, 2020 are classified as  current.
Loans  In 2020, due to the impact of Covid-19 pandemic, the  growth of loan disbursement in Indonesia’s banking  sector showed a declining trend.
Nevertheless, BNI’s loan  portfolio recorded a growth of 0.4% (net) and 5.3% (gross)  year-on-year.
The low growth rate of loan outstanding (net)  is attributable to the additional allowance for impairment  losses expected as a result of the implementation of SFAS  71 on January 1, 2020, in the amount of Rp12.9 trillion  after taking into account deferred taxes.
Loan outstanding  (gross), as the Bank’s core business, accounted for 60.8%  and 63.8% of total assets, respectively in 2020 and 2019.
BNI has rupiah- and foreign currency-denominated loans.
Rupiah-denominated loans (gross) accounted for the bulk  at 82.2% (2020) and 83.8% (2019).
Foreign currency- denominated loans (gross), most of which is in US Dollar  loans, contributed the remaining 17.8% and 16.2%,  respectively, in 2020 and 2019.    242 2020 Annual Report PT Bank Negara Indonesia (Persero) Tbk Uniting Energy to Revive the CountryFor the period up to December 31, 2020, the contractual interest rates on Rupiah-denominated loans are 5.5%-38.5%; US  Dollar (1.1%-11.0%); China Yuan (7.0%); and Japanese Yen (0.5%-2.1%).
In the previous year, the contractual interest rate  on BNI’s loans denominated in the four currencies are 5.0%-27.0%; 1.0%-11.0%; 7.0%; and 0.5-5.6%, respectively.
Based on loan types, BNI provides loans in the form of working capital loans, investment loans, consumer loans, syndicated  loan, employee loans and government program loans.
Working capital loans comprise of the largest portion of BNI’s (gross)  loan portfolio at 49.7% and 47.6% in 2020 and 2019.
On a cumulative basis, the loan portfolio is well diversified with the  contributions of investment loans (23.0%); consumer loans (17.7%) and syndicated loans (8.8%) in 2020.

Syndicated loans are loans granted to borrowers based on  joint financing agreement with other banks.
The percentage of BNI’s portion in the loan syndication, whereby BNI serves as  the lead accounted for 5.0%-83.3% in 2020 and 14.4%-93.0% in 2019.
Employee loans are loans to employees, bearing an interest rates of 3%-5% per annum, used for the purchase of housing  and other need, and with a tenor of between 1 year up to 20 years.
Payment of loan principal and interest is made by  deduction from the monthly salary.
Government Program loans consist of Food Security Loan (KKP), Two Steps Loan (TSL), Cattle Breeding Business Loan  (KUPS), and Plantation Revitalization Loan, which is partially or entirely funded by the Government.
By customer segment, the loan portfolio in 2020 is again dominated by the Corporate segment at 43.8%, followed by the  Consumer and the Small Business segments with 15.3% and 14.5%, respectively, the Medium Business segment with  11.5%, and the international (overseas branches) segment with 9.1% of the total loan portfolio.
On a consolidated basis,  subsidiaries contribute 5.9% of the total loan portfolio.

In implementing  loan write-offs, BNI’s Management prioritize debtors that are bankrupt and with legal issues, wherein maximum efforts  have been carried out.
In comparison to the total loans disbursed by the bank only, the loan write-off ratio is relatively low  at around 1.1%.
Meanwhile, loan recovery amounted to Rp2.0 trillion in 2020 with a recovery rate of 20.1%, lower than  48.2% achieved in 2019.
Government Bonds Government bonds are financial instruments that are classified within the low risk criteria but offer a competitive interest rate level while on the other hand also supports Government funding towards the State Budget.
As of December 31, 2020,  BNI posted Rp90.7 trillion in Government Bonds, an increase of 11.9% from the corresponding position in 2019.
BNI has  Rupiah- as well as foreign currency-denominated Government Bonds.
Rupiah-denominated Government Bonds amounted  to Rp69.2 trillion in 2020, or an increase of 21.4% from the corresponding position in the previous year at Rp57.0 trillion.
Meanwhile, foreign currency-denominated government bonds are valued at Rp21.5 trillion and Rp24.0 trillion in 2020 and  2019, respectively.
The Government Bonds account contributed 10.2% and 9.6%, respectively, of BNI’s total assets in 2020  and 2019.

The Bank’s Government Bonds portfolio included  Government Bonds derived from the recapitalization  program.
As at December 31, 2020 and 2019, the  recapitalization bonds amounted to Rp100 billion and Rp2.1  trillion, respectively.
The contractual interest rate of Government Bonds with  fixed interest rate in 2020 are 5.1%-12.0% for Rupiah-denominated bonds; 2.3%-4.4% (US Dollar); and 2.3%-3.3% (Singapore Dollar) per annum, compared with  5.5%-12.9%; 1.1%-5.9%; and 1.9%-3.3% the previous  year for the three respective currency denomination.
Meanwhile, interest rate per annum for Government  Bonds with floating interest rate is 4.0% in 2020 and 5.8%  the previous year.
Prepaid Taxes and Expenses  BNI booked prepaid taxes and expenses for the period  ending on December 31, 2020 of Rp1.0 trillion and  Rp2.8 trillion, respectively.
The respective corresponding  amounts in the previous year were Rp1.0 trillion and Rp2.6  trillion.
Equity Investments Net equity investments by BNI in associated entities  amounted to Rp813.1 billion in 2020, higher than the  corresponding position a year previously at Rp523.1  billion, attributable to the increase in fair value of equity  investment in 2020.
The increase is attributable to increases in a number of accounts, such as receivables as acquiring bank and foreclosed  assets.
Fixed Assets BNI booked net fixed assets valued at Rp27.4 trillion in 2020 from Rp26.6 trillion in the previous year, whereby none of  BNI’s entire fixed assets are placed as collateral.
The increase is mainly attributable to the implementation of SFAS 73,  whereby BNI recognized certain lease transactions meeting the criteria of SFAS 73 as leased asset.
As at December 31,  2020, these leased assets amounted to Rp1.6 trillion (net).
Moreover, the management believes that there is no decrease  in the value of BNI’s fixed assets within the current year since management believes that the fixed asset’s carrying amount  does not exceed the estimated value that can be recovered.
Fixed asset’s (net) contribution to BNI’s total assets in 2020  and 2019 are 3.1% and 3.1%, respectively.

Compared with the previous  position at Rp5.3 trillion, the increase in 2020 was in line  with the growth in the bank’s business that led to the  increase in obligations as an issuer bank (ATM) to Rp3.4  trillion, which is higher than in the previous year of Rp2.6  trillion.
Customer Deposits – Exclude Temporary Syirkah  Funds In the midst of tight liquidity conditions in the banking  industry during 2020, BNI posted a total third party fund  (TPF) of Rp647.6 trillion or grew 11.2% in 2020 from the  previous year’s position of Rp582.5 trillion.
Of the total TPF ,  69.2% of which was in the form of Current Account and  Savings Accounts (CASA) or equivalent to Rp448.3 trillion  in 2020.
Compared to the previous year, the amount of  CASA grew 13.9% or equivalent to Rp54.7 trillion, mainly  supported by a 16.9% increase in savings to Rp223.7  trillion.
This increase is in line with BNI’s policy to optimize  low cost third party funding sources.
BNI’s third party funds contributed the bulk to the  Bank’s liabilities at 86.8% and 84.6% to total liabilities,  respectively, in 2020 and 2019.

Mudharabah savings represent fund deposits by other parties that receive a share in the revenue derived by the Bank from  the use of such funds based on a pre-determined and pre-agreed ratio.
Mudharabah time deposits are investments by other  parties that receive a share in the income derived by a subsidiary from the use of such funds based on a pre-determined  and pre-agreed ratio.

PRIME LENDING RATE   Based on the Regulation of the Financial Services Authority (POJK) No. 6/POJK.03/2015 concerning Transparency and  Publication of Bank Reports as amended by POJK No. 32/ POJK.03/2016 and Bank Indonesia Regulation Number  7/6/PBI/2005 concerning Transparency of Bank Product  Information and Use of Customer Personal Data (State  Gazette of the Republic of Indonesia of 2005 Number  16, Supplement to the State Gazette of the Republic of  Indonesia Number 4475), Commercial Banks who carry out  conventional business activities in Indonesia are required  to report and publish the Prime Lending Rate (SBDK) in  Rupiah.
The prime lending rate implementation aims to provide  clarity to customers and facilitate customers in weighing  the benefits, costs and credit risks offered by the Bank.
In addition, publication of prime lending rates are intended  to improve good governance and promote healthy  competition in the banking industry, among others, through  the creation of better market discipline.
In addition, the prime lending rate is used as an indicator  of the amount of loan interest rates that will be charged to  customers applying for credit to the Bank.
Therefore, BNI  constantly updates the prime lending rate in accordance with the movement of the reference interest rate set  by Bank Indonesia.
In general, the prime lending rate is  calculated based on 3 (three) components, namely the  Cost of Funds for Credit (HPDK) arising from customer  fundraising activities, operating expenses incurred for  fundraising and lending and the profit margin component  set by the Bank in lending activities.
The prime lending rate  calculation does not take into account the risk premium  component of the debtor, the amount of which depends  on the risk assessment of each debtor.
Thus, the amount  of credit interest rate charged to debtors is not necessarily  the same as the prime lending rate.
BNI is required to report the prime lending rate calculation  to Bank Indonesia on a monthly basis and periodically  publish in the wider media.
The prime lending rate  calculation applies to types of corporate credit, retail credit, micro credit, and consumption credit (KPR and non-KPR).
However, Bank Indonesia submitted the classification of  corporate credit, retail credit and consumer credit (KPR and  non-KPR) based on the internal criteria used by each bank.
The following is the prime lending rate information that has  been determined by BNI in 2020: Description Prime Lending Rate per year Based on Business Segments Corporation Credit (%)Retail Credit (%)Micro Credit (%)Consumer Credit KPR  (%)Non KPR  (%) Prime Lending Rate 9.80 9.80 - 10.00 11.70 260 2020 Annual Report PT Bank Negara Indonesia (Persero) Tbk Uniting Energy to Revive the CountryFINANCIAL RATIOS Financial Ratio  2020 2019 2018 (%) (%) (%) CAPITAL     CAR-Tier I 15.7  18.6 17.4 CAR-Tier II 1.1  1.1 1.1 CAR (Credit, Market and Operational Risk) 16.8  19.7 18.5 Asset Quality    NPL Nett 0.9  1.2 0.8 NPL Gross 4.3  2.3 1.9 Adequacy ratio of provision for losses to non-performing loans 182.4  133.5 152.9 Profitability    ROA 0.5  2.4 2.8 ROE 2.9  14.0 16.1 Net Interest Margin 4.5  4.9 5.3 Efficiency    BOPO 93.3  73.2 70.1 CIR 44.2  43.9 42.5 Liquidity     LDR 87.3  91.5 88.8 RIM 75.4 86.6 84.6 Compliance    GWM (Rupiah) 5.4  6.7 6.5 Net Open Position 3.2  2.4 2.0 BMPK Percentage of violation  0.0  0.0 0.0 BMPK Percentage of exceedance  0.0  0.0 0.0 Capital Ratio  Capital Adequacy Ratio The capital adequacy ratio (CAR) in 2020 declined to 16.8%  compared with 19.7% in 2019.
The decline in the Bank’s  CAR was attributable to a number of factors, including  the increase in loan outstanding on the other hand while  experiencing a decline in retained earnings due to the  decline in income for the year and additional provision on  implementation of SFAS 71.
However, the Bank’s CAR  level is still far higher than the minimum level set by  regulators at 9.95% of the RWA for banks with category 2  risk profile.
Asset Quality Ratio  NPL Ratio  BNI recorded an increase in gross NPL from 2.3% in the previous year to 4.3% as at December 31, 2020, while net  NPL during the period declined from 1.2% to 0.9%.
It is undeniable that the Covid-19 pandemic has a  significant effect on BNI’s debtors, but to manage asset  quality, BNI implements a prudent productive asset  management policy in the midst of loan expansion,  including selectively choosing credit recipient sectors  supported by management of debtors those with  problems but still have the potential for improvement  through remedial and restructuring schemes to support  improvements to the debtor’s financial and business  conditions are key to NPL management at BNI.
Financial Review Management   Discussion & Analysis 261 Uniting Energy to Revive the Country2020 Annual Report PT Bank Negara Indonesia (Persero) Tbk Coverage Ratio BNI recorded a coverage ratio of 182.4% as at December  31, 2020, increasing significantly from 133.5% in 2019.
The increase in coverage ratio represents measures to  mitigate risk of non performing loans in the future.
Profitability Ratio Return on Asset Return on Assets (ROA) was 0.5%, declining from 2.4% recorded in the previous year.
The decline in ROA was  experienced industry-wide as bank profits declined in 2020.
Return on Equity In line with the declining growth in net income, BNI  recorded a Return on Equity (ROE) of 2.9% in 2020, much  lower compared to the previous year at 14.0%.
Net Interest Margin In line with the banking industry, Net Interest Margin  (NIM) at BNI declined from 4.9% in 2019 to 4.5% in 2020,  reflecting the decline in interest income in almost all  earning assets.
BOPO Efficiency Ratio In line with the Covid-19 pandemic that occurred throughout 2020, BNI also felt the challenge of increasing  operating expenses and decreasing operating income at  the industrial level.
Reflected by the increase in the ratio  of Operating Expenses to Operating Income (BOPO) in  the Indonesian banking industry, BNI’s BOPO (Operating  Expenses to Operating Income) ratio also increased to  93.3% in 2020 from 73.2% in 2019.
During 2020 BNI’s  operating income did not grow, while operating expenses  increased significantly by 155.6% in allowance for  impairment losses as a mitigation measure for industries  affected by Covid-19.
Cost to Income Ratio  Cost to Income Ratio (CIR) is a ratio that can measure the level of efficiency of operating expenses incurred to obtain  optimal income.
BNI’s CIR increased from 43.9% in 2019  to 44.2% in 2020 in line with less-than-optimal growth of  revenue as a result of the Covid-19 pandemic.
Liquidity Ratio Loan to Deposit Ratio (LDR)  The Loan to Deposit Ratio (LDR) is the ratio of loans  disbursed and deposits collected by banks.
BNI  recorded LDR of 87.3% in 2020, declining from 91.5%  in the previous year.
The decline mostly reflects a more  aggressive expansion of Third Party Funds compared with  the expansion in loans.
BNI’s LDR however is still within  the requirements of PBI No. 17/11/2015 for banks’ LDR to  be within the range of 78.0% - 92.0%.
Macroprudential Intermediation Ratio (RIM) BNI’s Macroprudential Intermediation Ratio was reported to have decreased to 75.4%, from 84.6% in the previous  year.
The achievement in RIM is below the regulatory  provisions of 84% - 94%, but there is relaxation in the form  of not being subject to disincentives if it is outside the  specified range.
Compliance Ratio  Statutory Reserves BNI consistently maintain an optimal level of liquidity to support daily operations and comply with Bank Indonesia  regulations through the statutory reserve requirement  (GWM).
In 2020, BNI maintain Rupiah GWM of 5.4%  and Foreign Currency GWM of 4.0%, compared to the  previous year’s position of 6.7% and 8.0%, respectively.
BNI’s Statutory Reserves (GWM) is in accordance with  Bank Indonesia Regulation (PBI) No.15/15/PBI/2013  dated 24 December 2013 concerning Minimum Statutory  Reserves for Commercial Banks in Rupiah and Foreign  Currency for Conventional Commercial Banks which have  been amended several times, the last one through the  Regulation of Members of the Board of Governors (PADG)  No. 22/10/PADG/2020 which comes into force on 1 May  2020.
Net Open Position For the period that ended on December 31, 2020, BNI  recorded Net Open Position (NOP) of 3.2%, higher  the corresponding position the previous year at 2.4%.
Nevertheless, this figure is still far below the maximum  level set by BI through PBI No. 5/13/PBI/2003 on Net Open  Position for Commercial Banks, which subsequently been  amended several times, the last through PBI No. 17/5/ PBI/2015, of 20% from total capital.  262 2020 Annual Report PT Bank Negara Indonesia (Persero) Tbk Uniting Energy to Revive the CountryCOMMITMENTS AND CONTINGENCIES An Broadly speaking, fluctuations in the movement of committed and contingent  posts are in line with credit growth, given that debtors are increasingly optimizing the use of BNI’s various products and  services with competitive features. 264 2020 Annual Report PT Bank Negara Indonesia (Persero) Tbk Uniting Energy to Revive the CountryDERIVATIVES AND HEDGING FACILITIES   BNI conducts derivative transactions for both the Bank’s and the customer’s interests.
As of December 31, 2020, BNI  conducted USD-IDR Cross Currency Swap (CCS) transactions recording a total asset value of USD37 million.
In addition  to CCS transactions, BNI also conducts Interest Rate Swap (IRS) transactions with a total asset value as of 31 December  2020 of USD 238 million.
CCS and IRS transactions are carried out by considering market conditions and portfolios held in  anticipation of currency movements and interest rates that could potentially harm the Bank.
In conducting its business, BNI conducts derivative financial instrument transactions, such as foreign currency forward  contracts, foreign currency swaps, interest rate swaps and spot transactions to manage exposure to market risks such as  currency risk and interest rate risk.
Derivative financial instruments are recognized in the consolidated statement of financial  position at fair value.
Any increase in fair value of derivative contracts is recorded as an asset when the fair value is positive  and as a liability when the fair value is negative.
Derivative receivables and payables are classified as financial assets and  liabilities at fair value through profit or loss.
Any gains or losses arising from changes in fair value are recognized in the  consolidated statement of income.
The fair value of derivative instruments is determined based on discounted cash flows and broker’s quoted price models  for other instruments with similar characteristics.
Foreign currency futures contracts, foreign currency swaps and cross  currency swaps and interest rate swaps are made for funding and trading purposes.
In addition, in conducting business, BNI carries out transactions in derivative financial instruments such as foreign currency  forward contracts, foreign currency swaps, interest rate swaps and spot transactions for financing, trading and hedging  purposes.

BANK HEALTH LEVEL   The Bank’s Health Level (BHL) is the result of the Bank’s  risk and performance assessment.
The Bank Health  Level Assessment is carried out using the Risk-based  Bank Rating approach both individually as well as on a  consolidated basis.
The Bank’s health level is a means to  identify at an early stage the bank’s problems, determine  the future business strategy, formulate and implement corrective action over a bank’s weakness/problem,  provide the basis for the process of linking capital with  risk, as a basis for decision-making as well as to enhance  competitiveness.
Meanwhile, the Bank’s Health Level serves as a means for  determining the strategy and focus for supervision on the  Bank for the supervisory authorities.
The Bank’s health level rating is based on 4 (four) factors  as follows: 1.
Risk Profile  Risk Profile assessment is conducted by evaluating  the risks inherent in the bank’s activities and the  quality of risk management implementation on the 8  types of risk.
Management   Discussion & Analysis 267 Uniting Energy to Revive the Country2020 Annual Report PT Bank Negara Indonesia (Persero) Tbk 2.
Good Corporate Governance  Good Corporate Governance assessment evaluates  the quality of the Bank’s management over the  application of Good Corporate Governance principles. 3.
Earnings  Assessment of the Earnings factor covers the  evaluation of profitability performance, profitability  sources, profitability sustainability, and profitability  management. 4.
Capital  Assessment of Capital covers the evaluation of  capital adequacy and adequacy of capital structure  management.
At BNI, evaluation of capital adequacy is  related to the Bank’s Risk Profile.
The Bank Health Level (BHL) rating is reported to the regulator (OJK) every 6 months in June and December.
The COVID-19 pandemic has had an impact on the BHL  of BNI, although not significant.
This is evident in the BHL  rating of BNI for the period ending December 31, 2020, of  “Healthy”, which implies the following:  a.
The Bank’s condition was generally healthy, thereby  deemed able to withstand significant negative effects  from changes in business conditions and other  external factors.
The rating assessment factors (Risk Profile, GCG,  Profitability, and Capital) are generally good whereby if  weaknesses are apparent, then these weaknesses are  generally deemed insignificant.
BNI’s risk profile, as one of the factors in the BHL  assessment for December 31, 2020, is ranked at category  2 (low to moderate).
As a result of BNI’s risk profile which is at the Low to Moderate level and according  to calculations using the Internal Capital Adequacy  Assessment Process (ICAAP), the minimum CAR  according to the risk profile is 9.95%.
If you add a buffer  capital, namely Conservation Buffer 0% (valid up to March  31, 2022 with approval of OJK), Countercyclical Buffer  0% and Capital Surcharge 1.50%, the Minimum Capital  Adequacy Requirement (KPMM/CAR) ratio limit is 11.45%.
In 2020, BNI’s CAR of 16.8% has exceeded the specified  minimum limit.
PLEDGED ASSETS In the period ending December 31, 2020, there are no  pledged assets of BNI.
IMPACT OF INTEREST RATE CHANGES TO  BANK PERFORMANCE   Throughout 2020, BI has cut its benchmark interest rate  five times to reach its lowest level in history, namely to  3.75% as of November 19, 2020.
The incessant cuts in the  benchmark interest rate are the response of the monetary  authority to the economic conditions affected by the  Covid-19 pandemic.
BI has cut interest rates by a total of  125 basis points (bps) in 2020.
The Board of Governors Meeting (RDG) of Bank Indonesia  on 16-17 December 2020 decided to maintain the BI  7-Day Reverse Repo Rate (BI7DRR) at 3.75%, the Deposit  Facility rate at 3.00%, and the Lending Facility interest rate  at 4.50%.
This decision is consistent with forecasts for  low inflation and maintained external stability, as well as  efforts to support economic recovery.
Bank Indonesia also  strengthens policy synergies and supports various further  policies to build optimism for national economic recovery,  through opening up productive and safe economic sectors for Covid-19, accelerating fiscal stimulus, channeling  bank credit from the demand and supply side, continuing  monetary and macroprudential stimulus, and accelerate  economic and financial digitization.
The decline in the benchmark interest rate had an impact  on the condition of the national banking system, which was  under significant pressure on the decline in the net interest  margin (NIM).
The push to lower lending rates to support  Indonesia’s economic growth at a time when inflation is  more under control is gaining the right momentum.
This  has an impact on the decline in BNI’s NIM to 4.5% in 2020,  compared to 4.9% (2019) and 5.3% (2018). 268 2020 Annual Report PT Bank Negara Indonesia (Persero) Tbk Uniting Energy to Revive the CountryGROWTH OF FEE BASED INCOME  BNI recorded Rp11.9 trillion in fee-based income in 2020, an increase of 4.5% from 2019 which amounted to Rp11.4 trillion.
The increase was dominated by 4 (four) banking activities, including ATM e-channels, Trade Finance, marketable securities  and forex trading.
In the midst of the Covid-19 pandemic, ATM e-channel and trade finance could grow by 7.0% and 8.4%,  respectively.
A significant increase occurred in non-recurring fee income, namely marketable securities and forex trading,  which grew significantly in 2020 by 43.2% and 41.3%, respectively.

This is shown by BNI’s ability  to meet all obligations due on time, both for payment of  principal debt or interest expense.
The banking financial  ratios to measure BNI’s liquidity and solvency are as  follows: Ability to Pay Short-Term Debt (Bank  Liquidity)  BNI’s ability to meet its short-term obligations is ensured  through good liquidity management.
To improve its short- term liquidity resiliency, BNI maintains adequate liquidity  by managing a number of indicators that include Primary  Reserve (Mandatory Reserves and Cash), Secondary  Reserve (liquidity reserves), and Liquidity Coverage Ratio  (LCR) in accordance with the regulator’s provisions.
LCR is a ratio that compares the amount of High Quality  Liquid Assets (HQLA) and the estimated total net cash  outflow for the next 30 (thirty) days in a crisis scenario.
In December 2020, BNI’s LCR reached 224.2% (bank  only) and 223.6% (consolidated), above the regulator’s  stipulation that LCR compliance is at least 85% up to  March 31, 2021 or during the banking relaxation period.
In managing liquidity for a longer period of time (1 year),  BNI maintains a Net Stable Funding Ratio (NFSR) by increasing the stability of bank funding according to the  composition of assets and administrative accounts.
NSFR  is the ratio of the amount of Available Stable Funding to  the amount of Required Stable Funding.
As of December  2020, BNI’s NSFR was 143.7% (bank only) and 149.4%  (consolidated), above the regulatory limit of 100%.
Ability to Pay Long-Term Debt (Bank  Solvency)  BNI’s Capital Adequacy Ratio (CAR), or the ratio of capital  to risk-weighted assets (RWA), decreased to 16.8% in  2020, compared to the capital adequacy ratio in 2019 of  19.7%.
Despite the decline in CAR, BNI’s capital structure  still has the capability to balance credit risk, market risk  and operational risk, where the ratio is higher than the  minimum capital adequacy ratio set by the regulator.
LOAN COLLECTIBILITY  BNI’s Non-Performing Loan (NPL) ratio increased to 4.3%  in 2020, from 2.3% in 2019.
However, net NPL improved  from 1.2% in the previous year to 0.9% in 2020.
Pressure  due to Covid-19 pandemic was a factor in the increase  of non-performing loan ratio at BNI.
However, BNI has  mitigated this risk by providing adequate provision for  non-performing loans, as indicated by an increase in the  coverage ratio from 133.5% in 2019 to 182.4% in 2020.
LOAN RESTRUCTURING  Loan restructuring is carried out on debtors who still have business prospects and is carried out selectively according  to the debtor’s ability.
The amount of restructured loans  at the end of 2020 reached Rp148.9 trillion, an increase of  287.8% compared to the previous year, with the following  details: 1.
Extension of loan tenor to a total of Rp32.4 trillion of  loans, up by 720.7% from the previous year. 2.
Reduction of loan interest rate to a total of Rp45.6 trillion of loans, up by 234.1.4% from the previous  year. 3.
Extension of loan tenor, reduction of loan interest rate and other forms of restructuring to a total of Rp71.0  trillion of loans, up by 241.0% from the previous year.
Based on collectibility as of December 31, 2020,  restructured loans were classified as current at 77.2%,  doubtful at 14.2% and non-performing loans (NPLs) reaching 8.5%.
In terms of currency, 90.5% of the  restructured loans were denominated in Rupiah, with the  remaining denominated in USD and SGD.

In terms of capital management, the Bank considers  factors such as: optimalizing capital return to shareholders, maintaining a balance between higher profits and gearing ratios  as well as the security provided by a healthy capital position.
It is carried out because BNI has a strong commitment to  maintain its capital structure composition in accordance with applicable provisions and does not violate the minimum limit  provisions applied by the Financial Services Authority (OJK) as a banking regulator.
Details of Capital Structure Referring to Basel III regulations in relation to capital requirements, BNI recorded 2.7% increase in RWA for credit risk, market risk, and operational risk, from Rp598.5 trillion in 2019 to Rp614.6 trillion by the end of 2020.
BNI has a strong  commitment to manage a healthy capital structure to support maximum business growth.

COMPARISON OF TARGETS AND REALIZATION AND PROJECTIONS FOR 2021 Achievement of Targets In 2020 The global economic slowdown due to the Covid-19 epidemic have an indirect impact on BNI’s overall growth; this situation  has been predicted  by BNI since last year and has taken preventive measures to survive amid the tight competition.
In  December 2020, BNI’s profit decreased by 78% compared to last year, namely Rp15.5 trillion in 2019 to Rp3.3 trillion in  2020.
BNI’s assets grew by 5.4% from Rp845.6 trillion in 2019 to Rp891.3 trillion in 2020, this growth in assets was supported  by the growth of Placements with Other Banks and BI by 28.4% to Rp61.3 trillion, which was followed by growth of  Government Bonds by 11.9% to Rp90.7 trillion, and an increase in loans (gross) of 5.3% to Rp586.2 trillion. 2020’s Strategic Policies 2020’s Target2020’s Realization  (Audited)Remarks 1.

TRANSACTIONS WITH RELATED P ARTIES In the normal course of its business, BNI conducts transactions with parties that are related through  ownership and/or management relationships.
All  transactions with related parties are conducted in  accordance with the agreed upon policies and terms.
BNI and its Subsidiaries conduct transactions with related  parties as defined in PSAK 7 regarding “Related Party  Disclosures” and Bapepam-LK Regulation No.
KEP-347/ BL/2012 dated June 25, 2012 concerning “Guidelines for  the Presentation and Disclosure of Financial Statements of  Issuers or Public Companies”, and are defined as: 1.
Companies under the control of BNI and its  Subsidiaries;  2.
Associated companies; 3.
Investors who have voting rights, which give them a  significant influence; 4.
Companies under the control of investors who have  voting rights, which gives the investors a significant  influence; 5.
Key employees and family members; and 6.
Entities that are controlled, jointly controlled or  significantly influenced by the Government, namely  the Ministry of Finance or the Regional Governments  who are the shareholders of the entity.
The provision of funds to  related parties is still in accordance with the maximum  threshold for lending in accordance with the POJK No.  32/POJK.03/2018 concerning the Legal Lending Limit  (BMPK) for Commercial Banks, namely a maximum of  10% of the Bank’s Capital.
In 2020, BNI provided funds to  related parties, namely BNI Syariah amounting to Rp2.9  trillion; BNI Asset Management of Rp1.6 trillion, and  BNI Multifinance of Rp644 billion.
Cumulatively, BNI has  conducted transactions with related parties based on the  equitable and fair principles.

BNI’s biggest contribution as  a taxpayer is fulfilling the Corporate Income Tax obligations.
On the other hand, BNI plays an active role in cutting every  taxable object in carrying out its function as a tax deduction.
BNI is always on time in terms of payment of tax obligations on  Corporate Income Tax, Employee Tax, PPN and PBB.
BNI also submits tax liability documents such as annual and monthly  tax returns as well as liability documents to the regulator in a timely manner.

With regards to FATCA, BNI has implemented the  following steps: FATCABNI has been  registered with the  IRS since the end of  April 2014 Since  January 2015,  the Customer Due  Diligence process has  been carried out by  requiring prospective  customers to fill out  an additional account  opening formSince July 1, 2014,  the Customer Due  Diligence process  for individual  customers has  been carried out In 2015, additional  forms for  individual  customers were  included in the  account opening  form Next, through POJK No. 25/POJK.03/2019 dated  October 15, 2015 concerning Submission of Foreign Customer  Information Regarding Taxation to Partner Countries or  Partner Jurisdiction, BNI has also committed to take part in  compliance with FATCA provisions, which have registered  with the IRS as a financial institution that will implement  FATCA provisions.
At present compliance with FATCA is  part of the Customer Due Diligence process at BNI which  has been implemented since July 1, 2017.
Bank reporting  related to the POJK will only be conducted at the end of  April 2018 for domestic taxation, while for the purposes  of international agreements will first be reported every  August 1.
TRANSFER PRICING DOCUMENT Minister of Finance Regulation (PMK) No. 213/PM.03/2016  concerning Types of Documents and/or Additional  Information that Must Be Stored by Taxpayers Conducting  Transactions with Parties with Special Relationships, and  Procedures for Management.
This regulation intends to improve the quality of  documents prepared by taxpayers and increase  transparency.
Taxpayers also need to be more proactive  and ensure that the information needed to prepare master  documents and local documents is available in order to  comply with the provisions in accordance with applicable  regulations.
PT Bank Negara Indonesia, Tbk (BNI) as a  taxpayer who obeys and complies with all existing tax  regulations and has complied with these regulations.
Preliminary The Ministry of Finance issued a new regulation on  taxpayers required to make Transfer Pricing Documentation  (TP Doc).
This new TP rule complements the provisions  related to the application of the principle of fairness and  common business practice in transactions involving related  parties.
Based on the definition in Article 1 number 6 PMK-213/ PM.03/2016 it is stated that the transfer pricing document  is a document that has been violated by the taxpayer as  the basis for applying the principle of fairness and common  business Practices in determining the transfer price carried  out by the Taxpayer.
This regulation was issued in connection with the  provisions of the transfer pricing document, and did not  replace the applicable regulation to regulate the principle  of fairness and common business practices, namely DJP Regulation No.
PER- 43/PJ/2010 as last amended by DJP  Regulation No.
PER-32/PJ/2011 concerning the Application  of Principles of Fairness and Common Business Practice in  Transactions Between Taxpayers and Related Parties.
Types of Documents That Must be  Organized Based on these regulations, taxpayers are required to  maintain and keep 3 (three) levels of documents consisting  of: 1.
Local Documents; and 3.
Reports by Country. 290 2020 Annual Report PT Bank Negara Indonesia (Persero) Tbk Uniting Energy to Revive the CountryThe aforementioned transfer pricing document must be  submitted in Indonesian.
However, taxpayers who have  obtained permission to keep books in foreign languages  and currencies other than Rupiah can produce documents  in English accompanied by transfer pricing documents in  the Indonesian language.
Subjects Required to Make Transfer  Pricing Document Parties that are required to make Transfer Pricing   Document can be grouped into 2 (two), namely: 1.
Those who are required to produce master documents  and local documents; and 2.
Those who are required to produce master documents, local documents and reports per country.
Impact of the Regulation to the Bank  In terms of implementing regulations related to Transfer Pricing, BNI has disclosed transactions with subsidiaries  and other related parties in accordance with applicable  regulations.
In terms of evaluating arms length transactions  or the reasonableness of BNI transactions with related  parties, the Bank uses the services of a Tax Consultant,  PT.
Multi Utama Consultindo (MUC), to conduct an  assessment.
Based on the results of the assessment  carried out, all transactions conducted by BNI with related  parties have met the specified fairness limit.
ACCESS TO FINANCIAL INFORMATION  FOR T AXATION PURPOSES Preliminary  The Automatic Exchange of Financial Account Information  or (AEOI) is the G20 countries’ plan and was initiated  by the Organization for Economic Cooperation and  Development (OECD) regarding a system that supports  the exchange of taxpayer account information between  countries.
With this system, taxpayers who have opened accounts  in other countries will be tracked directly by their home  country’s Tax Authorities.
AEOI has a new global standard  that will be useful to reduce the chance of avoiding tax  payments.
The AEOI work system is the exchange of financial data  of foreign nationals living in a country.
The exchange of  financial data is not done arbitrarily, but rather is carried out  between the tax authorities in each country.
Every country  that has joined the AEOI system will send and receive  pre-agreed information every year without having to submit  special requests.
In Indonesia itself, with the presence of AEOI, the  Directorate General of Taxes can supervise and explore  potential taxation through banking transactions or other financial institutions conducted by taxpayers abroad and  developed so that it applies to taxpayers in the country.
It  is done to strengthen the database which so far has limited  access so that it is expected that the potential of state  revenue from the tax sector can be maximized.
Scope  In accordance with Law No. 9 of 2017 concerning Determination of Government Regulation in Lieu of  Law Number 1 of 2017 concerning Access to Financial  Information for Taxation Purposes, the scope of access to  financial information is divided into 2 (two), namely: 1.
Exchange information for the benefit of international  agreements or foreign customers 2.
For the benefit of Domestic Tax or Domestic Customers in the context of implementing Tax  Regulations.
Reporting Subjects and Provider of  Financial Information  Based on Law No. 9 Year 2017, Financial Institutions (FI)  that are obligated as reporting subjects are as follow: Financial Institution by Sector Banking Capital Market InsuranceCommodity Futures  TradingCooperatives Commercial banks Securities Underwriting General and Sharia  Insurance CompaniesFutures Broker Deposit and Lending Cooperative BPR Broker-Dealer (PPE) Sharia Life and Life Insurance CompanyFutures Broker Clearing Member Islamic Bank Investment Manager (MI) Sharia Reinsurance & Reinsurance Company Custodian Bank Registrar Bureau Other Material Financial Information Management   Discussion & Analysis 291 Uniting Energy to Revive the Country2020 Annual Report PT Bank Negara Indonesia (Persero) Tbk CHANGES IN LAWS AND REGULATIONS WITH SIGNIFICANT IMPACT ON THE BANK  There were a number of changes in laws and regulations during 2020 with significant impact on BNI on a consolidated  basis, as follows: Changes in Laws and Regulations No.

PSAK 71 requires that financial reporting is based on calculations that take into account past, present and future conditions.
The objective of this PSAK is to establish financial reporting principles for financial assets and liabilities that are relevant and useful for financial reporting users to assess the amount, timing and uncertainty of the entity’s future cash flows.
Has a significant impact on financial instrument classification and on the method to establish the provision for expected credit loss. 2 PSAK 73: Leases PSAK 73 “Leases” establishes the principles for recognizing, measuring, presenting and disclosing an entity’s leases.
PSAK 73 is effective since January 1, 2020.
PSAK 73 implies the recognition of the Right to Use Leased Assets and Liabilities.
Has a significant impact on the leased assets, whereby the Bank recognizes leased assets and lease liabilities that meet the classification of PSAK 73.

Internal  factors include BNI’s ability to mobilize and allocate  resources and maintain and develop its core capabilities  which are important factors in anticipating and taking  business opportunities from existing external conditions.
External factors that affect the prospects for the Bank’s  business are economic, political, social, technological,  environmental and regulatory conditions.
In general, global  economic conditions are predicted to improve in the future,  supported by increased mobility and policy stimulus in  various countries.
The speed of global economic recovery  will also be influenced by progress in handling Covid-19,  especially the implementation of vaccination; increased  mobility; magnitude and speed of policy stimulus;  conditions in the financial and corporate sectors; as well as  the economic structure of a country.
The domestic economy has begun to improve in semester  II 2020 and is predicted to continue to strengthen in  2021.
Developments in a number of early indicators up to  the end of December 2020 confirm the direction of this  recovery, such as strengthening consumer confidence  and expectations regarding income, job availability and  business activities.
The prospect of speed of recovery  will be heavily influenced by vaccinations and public  discipline in implementing the Covid-19 protocol, which is a  prerequisite for the national economic recovery.
In addition, various policies to promote economic recovery  need to be implemented, namely (i) opening up productive  and safe sectors nationally and in respective regions, (ii)  accelerating fiscal realization, (iii) increasing bank credit  from the demand and supply side, (iv) the continuation of monetary and macroprudential stimulus, and (v)  the acceleration of economic and financial digitization,  particularly in relation to the development of MSMEs,  are also factors affecting the prospects for domestic  economic recovery.
With these various supporting factors,  Indonesia’s economic growth in 2021 is estimated to grow  in the range of 4.8%-5.8%.
Bank credit growth is predicted to improve in 2021 in line with improving business conditions.
The results of the  Banking Survey also showed an increase in the need for  financing and plans to apply for loans, issuance of bonds and stocks, and domestic debt in the next 3-6 months.
Lending will also remain conducive with low interest rates,  abundant liquidity, improved credit requirements (lending  standards), and the extension of the credit restructuring  program by OJK, while still applying the principle of  prudence and avoiding moral hazard. 2019-2025 LONG-TERM STRATEGY   In order to achieve BNI’s targets and objectives in the year  2025, BNI has formulated a Business Strategy as well as  a Functional Strategy, which are complementary to each  other.

CREDIT MONITORING  BNI monitors the debtor’s credit and industry conditions  as well as intensively carries out loan collection so as  to create quality asset growth.
This type of monitoring  is carried out by, among others, seeing the business  conditions both indirectly (online) as well as directly, if  needed, by continuing to adhere to the health protocols,  reviewing the debtor’s loan eligibility, and monitoring the  debtor’s loan payment obligations.
In principle, this loan  monitoring process is based on the assessment of the 3  (three) pillars within the OJK provision on productive asset  quality.
In the banking business segment, the monitoring process  uses a watchlist system that is used to monitor the  debtor’s loan performance and determine the steps  needed to prevent the debtor’s credit quality to deteriorate.
BNI also has an Early Warning System (EWS) device in  place and determine the action needed to handle the debtor to ensure that the credit quality will not deteriorate.
Meanwhile, credit monitoring in the consumer segment is  carried out by: 1.
Segmentation of billing based on credit card behavior  score, i.
historical analysis of transactions and  payment of debtor bills.2.
Priority of billing based on institution segmentation warning list for BNI Fleksi. 3.
Increasing collection productivity through the implementation of the Performance Collection  application for consumer credit products at centers  and branches. 4.
Special monitoring for large debtors (maximum credit of more than Rp1 billion). 5.
BNI Fleksi and Griya credit monitoring strategies•	 Submission	on	increase	in	credit	quality	to	 centers/branches •	 Adjustment	to	the	debtor	due	date	based	on	 payment behavior •	 Submission	of	Pending	Buyback	Guarantee	list	to	 related developer 6.
Credit card monitoring strategies, namely through SMS Blast, letters, visits and telephone calls.
LOAN SETTLEMENT AND RECOVERY  In 2020, the global economic uncertainty, which among others was caused by the trade war and the Covid-19  pandemic, significantly impacted the domestic economy  and the banking industry’s performance.
To deal with the  current economic situation, the banking industry continues  to prioritize prudent principles in managing business and  loan portfolio risks.
BNI’s strategy namely comprised of  providing loans to customers with good loan quality, a  prudent credit process and stringently loan monitoring.
Loan recovery and settlement strategy continues to be  carried out to strengthen BNI’s financial fundamentals  and maintain credit quality by, among others, improving  coverage ratio and optimally handle problem loans.
Problem loans are generally handled through two  strategies, namely loan recovery and settlement.
Loan Recovery is carried out through: 1.
Restructuring (Restructuring, Reconditioning,  Rescheduling) of debtors that face difficulties in paying  their debts but continue to have the prospects and  deemed cooperative; 2.
Instalments/Repayment through a strategic investor; 3.
Voluntarily sell collateral or execution of mortgage  rights; 4.
Foreclosed Assets and Temporary Bank Investment; 5.
Cooperate with third parties as an advisor or as a  lawyer. 6.
Efforts to apply a “non-conventional” scheme within the context of recovering a problem loan and  improving credit quality. 306 2020 Annual Report PT Bank Negara Indonesia (Persero) Tbk Uniting Energy to Revive the CountryMeanwhile, the Settlement Strategy is applied to the  debtor deemed to no longer possess prospects.
Loans that  are already written off will constantly strive to be settled so  as to reduce the Bank’s loss through: 1.
Debt settlement through a strategic investor; 2.
Voluntarily sell collateral or execution of mortgage rights; 3.
Strengthen digitization by improving BNI Collateral Auction website and application to optimize the use  and marketing of Consumer and Business Banking  segments distressed loan assets that can be also be  accessed by the General Public.  4.
Legal action through collection towards a guarantor over a personal guarantee (PG) and company  guarantee (CG), execution of a mortgage right/ fiduciary, litigation, bankruptcy and civil suits. 5.
Efforts to apply a “non-conventional” scheme so as to accelerate the settlement of non-performing loans and improve the chances for a recovery in order to  minimize the Bank’s losses. 6.
Subrogation.
The handling of distressed loans for consumer loans is  carried out through two strategies, namely loan recovery  and settlement.
The loan recovery and settlement strategy  carried out includes: 1.
Asset Quality Improvement and Recovery Acceleration  Program towards debtors facing difficulty in fulfilling  their obligations but still possess the prospects and  deemed worthy. 2.
Consumer Loan Asset Quality Improvement & Recovery Acceleration Program specifically for debtors  affected by Covid-19. 3.
Optimizing use of buyback guarantee (BNI Griya) and Collateral Auction Website. 4.
Optimizing Legal Action Collection (simple suit,  Cessie, summons, bankruptcy, and JPN). 5.
Loan settlement through NPL debt transfer and write-off (cessie-transfer or sale of bank claims towards  debtors or other parties in accordance with the criteria  determined by the Bank). 6.
Loan settlement through third party cooperation in the sale of distressed collateral assets (Property Agents).  2020 PERFORMANCE  Selective Productive Asset Growth  The Coronavirus Disease 2019 (Covid-19) pandemic that  occurred throughout 2020 has caused the global economy  to contract as a result of the lockdown occurring in most  countries.
This lockdown policy resulted in restricted global  mobility that further led to a decline in consumption, a  halt in the production process and declining global trade volumes.
A number of international organizations have  predicted 2020 global economic growth to contract to a  level of -5.2% to -3.7% (y-o-y).
Although the Covid-19  pandemic has yet to end, many countries have gradually  revived economic activities but others continue to apply  the lockdown to protect their citizens.
Towards the end  of 2020, the global economy’s recovery has once again  gradually move up to levels seen prior to the pandemic  with the level of activities that continued to maintain the  health protocols.
Against this backdrop, BNI established a policy to continue  to strengthen business expansion in selected corporate  markets and commercial segments in selected sectors  to maintain the growth of productive assets.
BNI also optimizes supply chain and cross selling, as an important  element in achieving quality credit growth through a  deep assessment process on the parent account (Anchor  Company).
Throughout 2020, BNI was able to register loan growth of  5.3%, or valued at Rp586.2 trillion, which simultaneously  marks the stability of the speed of the bank intermediary  functions amidst the challenging economic conditions.
This achievement is backed by the Bank’s efforts to carry  out improvements and credit risk management to instill  improved growth by continuing to apply prudent principles  amidst the Covid-19 pandemic.
BNI ensures that the credit  quality continues to be maintained through synergies  among the business units.
As a result, BNI is able to  maintain credit quality with achieving a non-performing  loan (NPL) ratio at a level of 4.3%.
Credit Risk Management Strategy The Bank’s various strategy and policy was able to register loan growth of Rp586.2 trillion in 2020.
This loan  growth was achieved by consistently applying prudent  principles whereby, despite the increase in Non-Performing  Loan (NPL) to 4.3%, was balanced with the increase in  allowance for impairment losses (CKPN) of Rp27.3 trillion,  which is in line with the implementation of PSAK 71 in  2020 and mitigation of risks associated with the impact of  the Covid-19 pandemic by sufficiently provisioning for non  performing loans.
BNI also applied a strategy that selectively expanded  to sectors with low risk and are main players in these  regions.
Moreover, BNI also conducted restructuring and  remedial for non-performing debtors that continue to  have the potential to improve financially and operationally.
Absolute NPL (Bank only) increased from Rp11.9 trillion in  2019 to Rp23.5 trillion in 2020.
Subsequently, gross NPL ratio amounted to 4.3% in 2020 with net NPL at 0.9% in  2020.
BNI continues to show its commitment to maintain  Credit Risk Management Management   Discussion & Analysis 307 Uniting Energy to Revive the Country2020 Annual Report PT Bank Negara Indonesia (Persero) Tbkthe quality of the loans disbursed amidst the Covid-19  pandemic’s impact. 2021 STRATEGY AND WORK PLAN By taking into account changes to business conditions and the economy as well as the Covid-19 that continues to  linger, BNI established the 2021 strategic policy and work  plan for the Risk Management Sector as follows:  1.

HUMAN CAPITAL ARCHITECTURE BNI Human Capital Architecture is a policy architecture  that leads to the Employee Value Proposition (EVP),  namely “Together making BNI the best place to contribute,  learn and grow”.
Emphasis on the phrase Together  indicates that employees and BNI are two entities that are  interrelated and inseparable in realizing BNI’s vision.
HC Architecture consists of organizations and employees  that are related to one another.
The organization has  goals to be attained, strategies for achieving these goals,  and a set of organizational culture that guides behavior.
Employees (people) are expected to be able to perform well in supporting the achievement of organizational goals,  to have competencies that are in line with the strategy, and  to behave in consistent with the organizational culture.
To support all the above-mentioned, the talent  management system incorporates career development  system (talent & succession), capability development system (learning & development), as well as appreciation  for the contributions made (reward and recognition).
Having employees widely spread across Indonesia, it is  imperative that the organization requires the support of  Information, Communication & Technology as the main  infrastructure to reach all employees throughout BNI  operational areas.
Moreover, the most important point in  the implementation of Human Capital policies is the active  role of leader across the organization to the smallest unit in  implementing the policies optimally. 310 2020 Annual Report PT Bank Negara Indonesia (Persero) Tbk Uniting Energy to Revive the Country GoalPerformanceCompetency BehaviorStrategy CultureInformation Com m unication Technology                 Inform ation Communication Technology Information Communication TechnologyLeadership                       Leadership                          LeadershipOrganizationPeople EVPTalent & Succession Learning & DevelopmentReward & Recognition BNI HUMAN CAPITAL MANAGEMENT STRUCTURE Human Capital management at BNI is led by the Director of Human Capital and Compliance.
There are two divisions  that manage Human Capital, namely the Human Capital Management Division, which has the authority to establish and  implement the operationalization of human resource management policies; and BNI Corporate University, whose main  function is developing employee capabilities.

IMPLEMENTATION OF HUMAN CAPITAL  STRATEGY IN 2020 Initially in 2020, BNI’s human capital strategy focuses  on improving employee capabilities through a number of  programs, including Enhancement Current Capabilities,  Job Shifting, Building New Capability and Global & Digital  Mindset.
Responding to the onset of Covid-19 pandemic that hit the  entire world, including in Indonesia, BNI has adjusted its  Human Capital management strategy to become Healthy &  Productive Employee.
Employee health is the main focus  of BNI this year, whereby employees who are maintained  in good health are expected to be able to be productive  and perform optimally to serve customer needs.
Supporting Healthy Employee Preventive 1.
Working environment  During the Covid-19 Pandemic, BNI’s working  environment was standardized according to Health  protocols so that employees, customers, debtors,  and other parties within BNI environment can carry  out activities safely and comfortably.
In promoting a  safe and comfortable working environment, BNI set  out several procedures, among others were cleaning  the building regularly by using disinfectant liquid,  setting up hand washing spaces, limiting the number  of employees, installing signs to maintain distancing,  checking body temperature on entrance by using face  recognition, and few other things. 312 2020 Annual Report PT Bank Negara Indonesia (Persero) Tbk Uniting Energy to Revive the CountryProtocol in the Work Area regarding Adaptation to New Habits Human Capital 2.
For Employees  During the Covid-19 pandemic, BNI has implemented  Work from Home (WFH), Work from Office (WFO),  Shift and Split Operations, to limit activities within  the BNI environment.
In case the employees were  required to undertake WFO and located in areas with  restrictions or high-risk zones, they were provided  with healthy, clean, and nutritious lunch and equipped  with health supplement.
This effort was aimed to  limit the activities of eating outside the office, thus  minimizing potential transmission of Covid-19 amongst  employees.
In addition, the management also gave  transportation assistance such as online taxi vouchers  and operational cars.
Moreover, the employees  can periodically take periodic antigen swab test to  continuously provide a sense of security at work.
Curative For employees who were exposed to Covid-19, BNI took  serious care in supporting their recovery from Covid-19.
The support given by the Company include providing  vitamin supplementation for employees who were  confirmed positive, providing independent isolation spots,  and assisting on financial support when the employees  needed special care for monitoring the condition.
Monitoring Specifically, BNI has established the Emergency Task Force  (ETF) team in the respective unit tasked with monitoring  the health of employees in the unit.
With the help of  technology, namely DigiHC, the ETF teams could get daily  data on the health conditions of employees and conduct  Management   Discussion & Analysis 313 Uniting Energy to Revive the Country2020 Annual Report PT Bank Negara Indonesia (Persero) TbkTo boost employee productivity, BNI also made  enhancement by implementing the Daily Planner as a  tool for monitoring daily work plans.
To accommodate  changes in work locations, including split operations and  work from home, the infrastructure of application was also  strengthened so that employees can access performance  management applications through mobile phones by using  DigiHC application.
Capability Development  Learning Programs During the Covid-19 Pandemic  Despite the pandemic situation, the employee capability  development strategy is still implemented with a number  of adjustments, especially in the learning delivery  mechanism.
The face-to-face method, which is initially one  of the primary methods, is now being adapted to a number  of alternative strategies including: •	 Adjustment	of	the	delivery	method	to	be	100%	digital	 compared to only around 20% previously.
The change presented its own challenges as it involves changing  the mindset and behavior of employees to learn  online, preparing the capabilities of facilitators to teach  online, and strengthening the capabilities of the digital  support infrastructure.
•	 Designing	gamification	learning	applications	to	 accelerate changes in employee behavior in learning  through a new learning experience that is different  from conventional learning.
•	 Organizing	a	webinar	series	through	the	Knowledge	 Supplement program which can be accessed through the BNI Corporate University Youtube channel.
Throughout 2020, there are 140 topics with various  themes ranging from business, operations, risk, to  lifestyle.

monitoring, especially for employees who are sick.
If  employees need special assistance, the ETF team is also  ready to coordinate and provide the support needed by  employees regarding their conditions.
Data on health conditions for all BNI employees is  integrated data that is reported daily to management as  part of BNI’s efforts to maintain employee health.
For  management, this can be the basis for making decisions  on the right strategy change in dealing with pandemic conditions, while for employees with daily monitoring it  makes employees feel fully cared for and supported by  BNI.
In the event that an employee is exposed, BNI also  actively pays attention to the 3T protocol or testing, tracing  and treatment.
Employees who are in close contact with,  and are in the same area with positive employees will be  tested so that if there are positive employees they can be  treated early on.
In addition to initiatives in employee monitoring, BNI also  has a Covid Ranger as a Change Agent in socializing a new  lifestyle, namely 3M or wearing masks, washing hands and  maintaining distance.
Apart from being carried out by Covid  Ranger, 3M socialization was also carried out through the  installation of banners & posters, stickers and through  webinars.
In addition to the Covid Ranger and ETF teams,  each line manager is also responsible for the health of all members of their respective team.
Supporting Productive Employee Enhancement Performance Management System Along with changes in ways of working in the pandemic era, it was necessary to make some adjustments to  the performance management system mechanism to  ensure that employee productivity can be maintained.
BNI continued to implement a performance management  system which consists of three aspects, namely goal  setting, performance driving and performance evaluation.
These three aspects were monitored regularly in two  cycles, namely the short cycle that was monitored every  quarter and the full cycle that was monitored annually.
In line with the implementation of new ways of working,  the Company applied flexible KPIs to measure the  performance of employees working from home.

Implementation of Other Programs in  Human Capital Workforce Planning & Recruitment In 2020, the workforce planning strategy was focused on  ensuring the availability of employees in selected positions  that become the focus of BNI’s business, in line with the  Bank’s revised business plan in response to the Covid-19  pandemic situation.
The target number of employees in  2020 remained stable with an increase in the composition  of employees in business origination roles to support the  achievement of BNI’s business strategy.
Realization of the number of employees was 27,202  or relatively lower than that of the previous year.
With  this number of employees, the employee productivity  measured based on the Earning per Employee indicator was Rp101 million/employee.
The realization of employee composition in business origination roles also reached  57%, or an increase compared to 55% achievement in  2019.
The increase in the employees composition in  business origination roles was driven by the increase in the  composition of the credit and funds segments in line with  BNI’s business strategy.
Even in a pandemic situation, BNI continued to recruit  through a number of recruitment channels according to the  objectives of the positions required.
The recruitment was  carried out to ensure sustainable employee regeneration.
Officer Development Program (ODP) is a recruitment  program for prospective officers, aiming to recruit fresh graduate from university to pursue a career at BNI.
Prospective officers recruited through this route will be  provided with structured program to improve soft skills  and hard skills for 1 year before occupying the designated  position.
Most of the employees recruited from this route  are prioritized for business origination roles, including  positions related to credit quality and other positions  that support BNI’s business strategy such as IT and Data  Analytics.
The number of employees recruited through this  route was 322 employees.

Talent Management To realize BNI’s vision and mission, BNI Human Capital is committed to manage BNI’s talents through the Talent  Management System.
Talent Management performed by  BNI consists of Talent Acquisition, Talent Classification,  Talent Development, Talent Mobility and Talent Retention.
All stages of talent management involve the role of the  Talent Committee that aims to ensure that the Talent  Management process can take place objectively and in  standardized manner.
In line with the objective of managing integrated human  resources, the talent management process implemented  at BNI focuses on preparing, developing, and retaining  employees while adhering to the Employee Value  Proposition (EVP).
BNI is committed to managing talent  consistently with a long term orientation.
A number of  talent management programs implemented in 2020 were  the following: Career Acceleration In line with the Company’s strategy, in which one of the focuses is to prepare the Company to compete in the  future, BNI provides opportunities for its best talents to  develop careers according to their capability and capacity  through a career acceleration program to occupy leadership  positions.
The career acceleration program is carried out with strict  selection with the aim of ensuring that employees who  participate in this program have qualified capabilities before  occupying the target position.
There are 2 (two) paths that  can be taken by employees, namely career acceleration  without going through the regular career path stages (skip  path), and career acceleration with a shorter period than  the usual (speed path).
This program shows to all BNI Hi-Movers that BNI  management does not fail to pay attention to the performance of all Hi-Movers wherever they are placed.
