Challenging targets and work environments of different  generations are challenges in shaping the team’s character in making the outlet I lead a profit center.
The opportunity to exchange ideas with the Regional Leaders, Deputy District Leaders and Branch Leaders as mentors stimulates new ideas and enthusiasm.

EIS & DSS, is part of the application architecture  that provides analytical applications and information  processing consisting of Regular Reports, Business  Intelligence, Dashboards, and Analysis. 2.
Data Warehouse & Big Data, which is an integrated interface that processes Data Extract, Transform,  Load (ETL) & Extract, Load, Transform (ELT) and data  management. 3.
Operational Processing, which is part of the application architecture that provides BNI business  operational applications consisting of 3 (three) sub  sections, namely: a.
Product Processing, the Bank’s main business  operations application.
Bank Management, application that supports the Bank’s main business operations.
Customer Management, an application used to  manage customer data/Bank user services.4.
Delivery Channel (Direct & Indirect Access), which  is part of the application architecture that provides  applications that facilitate the interaction of parties  related to the Bank directly (direct access) and indirect  (indirect access) by customers. 5.
Middleware or Enterprise Application Integration (EAI), is the integration of data/information between  applications. 6.
External Link, is part of the application architecture that provides applications that are connected with  third parties, both for business to business and  business to government connections.
Payment is a module for payment transactions,  money transfers and transaction settlement. 7.
Supporting Business Applicationsa.
Risk is a collection of risk management  applications.
Administration is a collection of Administrative  Applications and their supporters. 8.
Infrastructure, is an application that supports all Bank business operations and is closely related to IT  activities.

INFORMATION TECHNOLOGY  INFRASTRUCTURE  “BNI accelerates the provision of server  infrastructure by shifting our server  requirements from a conventional model towards a service-oriented infrastructure  model by adopting Cloud Computing  that is able to accommodate demands for Infrastructure as a Service (IaaS) and Platform as a Service (PaaS) for BNI’s  digital services in the future.
“ As a form of support for BNI’s various business activities,  BNI’s Information Technology infrastructure is required  merely to maintain the reliability and availability of BNI’s IT  services, but is also expected to constantly develop as a  strategic partner for BNI’s business initiatives.
Throughout  2020, BNI successfully upgraded its Core Banking &  Core Service infrastructure which to date serves as  the backbone for almost all of BNI’s digital services by  simultaneously improving Core Banking & Core Service  infrastructure capacity in order to improve the performance  of BNI’s digital services thereby ready to accommodate  BNI digital services innovation in future.
In facilitating innovation and business initiatives, BNI  optimizes the use of both public as well as private cloud  as a means of application deployment that is efficient in  terms of cost and time.
By utilizing BNI’s own cloud portal,  developers have a self-service portal that can be accessed at any time to fulfil server needs based on a catalogue that  is ready to use as needed.
Moreover, BNI has enhanced  its own cloud capability in support of the Platform-as-a- Service (PaaS) technology, namely technology that uses a  container to produce BNI‘s future digital service innovation  and as part of its support to implement DevSecOps within  BNI’s working environment.
To support the provision of products and services that are based on the Internet of Things (IoT) in the outlets,  BNI enhanced communication network capacity in the  outlets by adopting the Software Defined Wide Area  Network (SD-WAN) technology that is encrypted so  as to integrate the Internet network as BNI’s network  alternative that is safe, reliable, and cost-effective so as  to enhance outlet’s speed to access BNI’s application to  serve the customer.
Moreover, in adapting to the new  normal era, BNI’s Information Technology infrastructure  also actively participates to support the Work from Home  (WFH) and Split Office program by constantly improving  communications network capability and fulfill supporting  infrastructure for BNI’s personnel that allows them to contribute their best despite working from home or even  from offices that are situated in different locations.
INFORMATION SECURITY CONTROL In an effort to improve information security, in addition  to implementing a variety of safeguards that refer  to international standards, BNI also formed a special  organization (Information Security Unit) that combines  several units that have functions related to information  security to maintain independence and focus more on  evaluating, implementing, monitoring and improving  cybersecurity.
This Information Security Unit plays a role  in all activities related to information security at BNI,  including in the areas of governance, access control, and  business processes, and plays an active role in the field of  application development, operational information security  life cycle including digital forensic and incident handling  related to cyber-crime.
Proactive Cybersecurity is an important factor in gaining  customer trust so that BNI will always receive serious  attention for continuous development.
In implementing cybersecurity, BNI has adopted several international  frameworks and applicable regulations. 324 2020 Annual Report PT Bank Negara Indonesia (Persero) Tbk Uniting Energy to Revive the Country ISO 27001NISTCOBIT POJKIDENTITY PROTECT PLANRESPOND CHECKDETECT DORECOVER ACT To ensure business continuity from the threat of  cybercrime, BNI carried out the following efforts: 1.
Constantly implement governance, regulation and  compliance so that information security can function  well and in accordance with internal policy, prevailing  rules and regulations as well as best practices, 2.
Develop security aspects in every applications development by applying Secure SDLC framework,  3.
Implementing information security architecture towards data, application, endpoint, network and  security perimeter that is constantly carried out to  ensure that the principles of confidentiality, integrity,  and availability can function well,  4.
Implementing a multilayer of defense security device that is based on international standards that is applied  in national banks, 5.
Proactively monitor 24x7 against cyber threats, 6.
Work together with official state agencies (such as BI, OJK and BSSN), principal security apparatus and  other cybersecurity community to receive information  related to threats and weaknesses, latest technology  and products as well as receive support in the event  an incident occurs 7.
Educate employees to increase awareness of cyber security, 8.
Constantly educate awareness through Human Resource competency development programs.
In addition to the aforementioned matters, as well as  taking into account the current trends of cyber attacks,  which are increasingly widening towards customers, BNI  implements several safeguards on the customer side,  including:1.
Application of various mechanisms of customer  protection against fraud transactions caused by  malware banking and social engineering. 2.
Implementation of fake website detection in the name of BNI. 3.
Notification mechanism for customer transactions. 4.
Continual education to customers about self- protection through password security, internet banking  security, mobile banking security, transaction security  at ATMs and others.
With the direction of business development towards digital  banking, cybersecurity will continue to be developed in guarding banking service innovations so that aspects of  customer trust and comfort can always be maintained.

Information Technology Management   Discussion & Analysis 327 Uniting Energy to Revive the Country2020 Annual Report PT Bank Negara Indonesia (Persero) TbkINFORMATION TECHNOLOGY GOVERNANCE Application of IT governance is carried out by aligning the IT Strategic Plan with the Bank’s business strategy, optimize  human resources, utilizing IT, measuring performance, and applying effective risk management by continuing to meet the  provisions set by the OJK and Bank Indonesia.
Applying IT governance in BNI covers the following items: The Adequacy of   the IT Risk   Management ProcessAdequacy of IT   Policies, Standards   and ProceduresActive Supervision  Board of Directors &  Board of CommissionersInternal Control   System for the   Use of IT The use of IT in BNI is regulated through the policies, standards, and procedures that are applied consistently and  continuously in accordance with that prescribed within OJK Regulation No. 38/POJK.03/2016 dated December 1, 2016  and OJK Circular Letter No. 21/SEOJK.03/2017 dated June 6, 2017 on Applying Risk Management in Using Information  Technology by Banks that covers the aspects:  Security InformationCommunication  Network IT Service  Providers by BanksIT Operations Use of IT Service  ProvidersDevelopment &  Procurement Electronic Banking  ServicesManagement Disaster  Recovery Plan Selection of a good IT governance framework requires a balance between People, Process, and Technology aspects.
Based on these considerations, IT governance implemented in BNI adopts various scope of work that is in line with the area of IT  services in BNI.
Control Objectives For Information And Related Technologies (COBIT) Control Objectives for Information and Related Technologies (COBIT) is widely recognized as an IT management and IT  governance framework.
COBIT manages IT in meeting the needs of BNI’s stakeholders through the management of its  process groups and enablers, where business objectives are mapped to IT objectives, and their achievements and maturity  are measured.
In order to fulfill compliance with the Regulation of the Minister of BUMN No.
PER-02/MBU/2013, an IT  management assessment (IT Maturity assessment) has been carried out by an external consultant and based on the results  of the assessment, BNI’s IT Maturity Level has met the minimum needs with a score of 3.8 out of the minimum 3 set.
BNI IT uses the COBIT framework as a reference for its governance, among others due to the synergy between business  objectives and IT objectives, focusing on data and information, being able to flexibly follow the direction of the Bank’s work,  and can be used in conjunction with other framework standards. 328 2020 Annual Report PT Bank Negara Indonesia (Persero) Tbk Uniting Energy to Revive the CountryAWARDS IN  2020  Various efforts made by the Bank throughout 2020  obtained good results.

Information Technology Information  Library (ITIL) The Information Technology Information Library (ITIL) is a  standard framework for IT Service Management (ITSM),  which is used by BNI’s IT in aligning IT support services  to BNI’s businesses.
ITIL focuses on IT processes,  procedures, tasks and service levels to support the Bank’s  strategy, provide added value, and maintain IT competency  levels.
With ITIL, BNI’s IT operations have set baselines as  service benchmarks, as a basis for planning, implementing  and measuring their achievements.
International Organization For  Standardization 9001 (ISO 9001)  ISO 9001 is a quality management system standard  (Quality Management Systems) that is designed to  ensure that BNI can meet stakeholder demands while  complying with the needs of regulators regarding its  products and activities.
BNI IT has implemented ISO 9001  since 2007 with the scope of IT Operation and IT Security  Management.
BNI’s IT has successfully met the requirements to be  able to upgrade ISO 9001:2008 to ISO 9001:2015 by  establishing mechanisms and quality standards that focus  on Bank performance with a risk-based thinking approach  so that the IT unit will be more proactive in preventing and  reducing undesirable effects and always improving the  system on an ongoing basis (continuous improvement) and  can maintain ISO 9001:2015 certification.
Information Technology Management   Discussion & Analysis 329 Uniting Energy to Revive the Country2020 Annual Report PT Bank Negara Indonesia (Persero) TbkINFORMATION TECHNOLOGY  DEVELOPMENT PLAN New  Digital  Proposition Strive for   Operational ExcellenceGovernance Toward  Performance Innovative and Agile  OrganizationBNI IT  Strategic Direction To ensure the implementation of the application  development plan and support the corporate plan 2019- 2023, BNI established 4 (four) strategic directions for  IT, namely New Digital Proposition, Governance Toward  Performance, Strive for Operational Excellence, and  Innovative and Agile Organizations.
New Digital Proposition for IT utilization that answers how  digitalization can bring something of new value to its users.
This strategic direction encourages regular digital business  value creation, by providing recommendations in the form  of adjustments and development of new business models  based on emerging IT trends or through digital innovation.
Governance towards Performance to fulfill good  governance in order to encourage optimal performance,  including through effective prioritization, reliable portfolio  management, demand management and IT planning in line with business needs, and good synergy with all units and  subsidiary companies.
Strive for Operational Excellence to optimize operational excellence through digitalization and automation of  business processes while enhancing cybersecurity and  developing a sustainable operating model in a consistent  manner.
Innovative and Agile Organization to obtain an organization  that is adaptive to change and has the capability to deliver  deliverables quickly, including through a customer-centric innovation culture to meet customer needs precisely  and efficiently, with visionary mindset transformation  in IT strategy and planning, and application of Agile  methodology.
As a manifestation of the strategic direction above, and  also as part of an ongoing project planning system to meet  business needs for IT support, BNI implements an IT  Planning Session forum that brings IT work units together  with all units in BNI.
In the forum, all units discussed with  IT work units related to business needs and achievement  targets, as well as expectations in the future, both in  terms of development solutions, security, operational, data  processing, and reporting needs.
The IT Planning Session Forum can show the need for  application/architecture development to be initiated in 2021.

BNI DIGITAL ASSISTANT (BDA)   As time goes by, customer needs or wants and expectations continue to change.

Digital Service   In 2020, the Service Quality Unit strives to realize BNI’s strategy in improving the customer transaction  experience through the implementation of digital  services at all touch points.

Implementation of Health Protocol  Standard The role and responsibility of SQU as a policy maker for  service standards at Branch Offices/Outlets in relation to  health protocols during the pandemic is a form of company  compliance with regulations or policies of both central and  local government as well as a form of BNI’s social concern  for the community in preventing Covid-19 transmission.
BNI management continues to oversee all frontend  and backend officer activities through a series of health  protocols implementation, including: a) Protocol for the use of Personal Protective  Equipment (PPE) in each Branch Office/Outlet •	 Masks,	gloves,	hand	sanitizers,	thermo	guns	used	 by all frontliners are mandatory protocols to be  applied during service operating hours.
•	 Disinfectant	sprays	in	banking	halls	and	all	work	 areas •	 Installation	of	a	droplet	protection	acrylic	 board for each branch office/outlet to maintain  customer comfort in communicating and making  transactions with officers.
•	 Tissue	and	hand	sanitizer	to	facilitate	customers	 on transacting at an ATM •	 Every	marketing	officer	is	encouraged	to	use	 online communication media in conducting  marketing or advisory services to customers  (adjusted to customer conditions).
The officer will  make an appointment (schedule and location of  the meeting) while still paying attention to the  provisions of the PSBB for the local area if the customer still wants to meet face to face.
b) Implementation of Social/Physical Distancing  BNI implements capacity limitation standard for banking hall and queue management as one of the  Management   Discussion & Analysis 351 Uniting Energy to Revive the Country2020 Annual Report PT Bank Negara Indonesia (Persero) Tbk strategies for managing the number of customer queues  based on the Covid-19 protocol, as a reference or basis  for Branches/Outlets to ensure that incoming customer  queues to outlets run properly, orderly and according to  Covid-19 protocol.
Banking Hall Capacity Limit  Policies related to preventive measures of Covid-19 were also carried out by imposing restrictions on the number  of queues of customers at the banking hall.
Banking hall  capacity can only be filled up to a maximum of 50% of the  normal capacity.
When the incoming queue exceeds the  maximum capacity, each branch office/outlet is allowed  to add chairs and tents outside the banking hall.
Seating  arrangement in the waiting room is suited to the condition  and needs of each outlet by taking into account the  minimum 1 meter physical distancing measure.
Queue Management Operations •	 There	are	2	types	of	queue	numbers	to	manage	 incoming customers, namely arrival queue number and transaction queue number.
•	 The	arrival	queue	number	is	the	queue	number	used	 to manage incoming customer to remain in an orderly  manner in accordance with the customer arrival at an  Outlet/Branch.
•	 The	arrival	queue	number	can	be	issued	by	the	 security guard to the customer 30 (thirty) minutes  before the Outlet Operational Hours starts.
Security  officers are not allowed to provide arrival queue  numbers before the required hours.
•	 Arrival	queue	numbers	are	only	applied	before	 service operating hours.
After the Outlet opens and  during service operating hours, the queue number  for arrivals is not applied, the customer is simply provided with the transaction queue number.
•	 Transaction	queue	number	is	the	queue	number	 given by security guards to customers during service  operational hours according to the type of customer  transaction to be directed to CS/Teller.
c) Optimization of Security Officers  As a customer touch point, every security guard at Branch Offices and Outlets across all BNI Regional Offices is  required to inform customers that BNI provides security  and convenience for transactions at Branch/Outlet Offices  because BNI strictly applies the Covid-19 protocol.
•	 Security	officers	are	responsible	for	directing	 customers to wear masks if they wish to make transactions in the BNI area, both in banking halls and  ATMs.
•	 Measuring	the	customer’s	body	temperature	before	 entering the banking hall (maximum 37.5 °C) •	 Application	of	physical	distancing	rules	(keep	a	 minimum distance of 1 m) •	 Customer	queue	arrangement•	 Educate	customers	to	use	e-channels	as	an	 alternative medium for transactingd) Optimization of BNI Digital Assistant (BDA)  Officers  In order for customers to continue transacting in the  midst of a crowded queue Branch, every BDA officer  at the Branch Offices/Outlets is required to educate  customers to use BNI e-channel as an alternative  medium for transacting so that customers feel  comfortable of making transactions without having to  come to the Branches/Outlets.
•	 E-channel	education	to	customers •	 Directing	customers	to	divert	their	transactions	 via e-channel •	 Inviting	customers	to	experience	BNI	e-channel e) Awareness and Education of Branch  Operational Services in the Covid-19 Era  As a step in educating and providing information  regarding the implementation of health protocols at  BNI to ensure customer convenience in transacting  as well as a form of company compliance with BNI’s  provisions and concern for public financial activities  during the Covid-19 pandemic, BNI through its Service  Quality Unit also ensures that every Branch Office/ Outlet becomes the enabler of the Covid-19 protocol  education process to customers.
The educational  process is carried out by providing educational content  implemented in all Branch/Outlet Offices through the  available means or media of communication, including  announcement posters, banners, and screen monitors  in the banking hall.
Some of the educational content that has been  created, includes: •	 E	Booklet	of	Branch	Service	Operations	during	 Covid-19, •	 Educational	 Videos	of	New	Normal	Branch	Service	 Operations, •	 Educational	Videos	of	Health	Protocol	 Implementation at Branch Offices, •	 Educational	Videos	for	Social	Assistance	 Distribution during Covid-19 Period, •	 Animated	Videos	on	Switching	Transaction	to	 E-Channel, and others.
